# SDP-Constraining Normative Clause Inventory

Independent Phase-1 spec walk for `parse_sdp` pre-1.0 audit (audit pass #31).

This document is the **inverted-direction** spec inventory: every SHALL /
SHALL-NOT / MUST / MUST-NOT / "is forbidden" / defined-value-set clause
enumerated cold from the source specs, then later compared against the parser
in Phase 2. The direction is spec → parser, not parser → spec, to break the
confirmation bias that has kept the audit open for 30 passes.

Each row in the per-spec tables carries:
- the verbatim spec quote (≤3 sentences)
- a one-line summary
- a `SDP?` Y/N classification (Y = this clause constrains SDP content;
  N = RTP packet behaviour / RTCP / NMOS / device capability / receiver
  behaviour, with the reason)
- `Notes` for `AMBIGUOUS`, `[AES67-2013 wording]` (paywalled-revision flag),
  `scope: <intro clause>` (bullet-binding rule applied), `cross-ref: <spec>`

The inventory was assembled by 22 specialised spec-walker agents working in
parallel, each blind to the parser. After this Phase-1 sweep, the main thread
walks `parse_sdp.lua` and `spec/` to build a coverage map (Phase 2), then
writes a findings report (Phase 3) in the format defined by
`.claude/prompts/independent_audit.md`.

## Phase-1 Headline Observations

Items the agents surfaced that are worth threading into Phase 2 (each is a
candidate for a Direction A "SHALL not enforced" or Direction B "check without
SHALL" finding — but Phase 2 verifies against the parser before any of these
is treated as a finding):

1. **ST 2022-7:2013 never mentions SDP.** Not once. Any `parse_sdp` check that
   cites `ST 2022-7 §6` for an SDP attribute requirement is mis-cited. The
   correct cite for `a=group:DUP` is **RFC 7104** (and the receiver-coherence
   inference rolls up from ST 2022-7's "RTP header and payload shall be
   identical for each datagram copy", §6).
2. **ST 2110-30:2025 cites AES67-2023, not AES67-2018.** The audit-prompt's
   AES67-2018 paywall caveat was already understated — 2018 is no longer the
   current normative reference; 2023 is. Only AES67-2013 is on disk.
   Conclusions about audio packet-time / sample-rate / encoding SHALLs must be
   flagged `[AES67-2013 wording]` and treated as provisional until either 2018
   or 2023 is obtained.
3. **ST 2110-30:2025 cites RFC 8866, not RFC 4566.** `parse_sdp`'s CLAUDE.md
   names RFC 4566 as the SDP base. RFC 8866 obsoletes 4566 with several
   normative changes (notably k= line is obsoleted; v4 multicast c= line now
   mandates `/ttl`; v6 multicast c= explicitly forbids TTL).
4. **ST 2110-10:2022 §8.2 has a likely citation typo** — text reads "IETF RFC
   7272" where context (clock signalling) requires RFC 7273. Flagged
   `AMBIGUOUS` in the inventory; should be reported to SMPTE editorially but
   does not change the parser's correct citation.
5. **ST 2110-40:2023 explicitly forbids `a=group:FID`** for ANC streams. If the
   parser doesn't enforce this, it's a Direction-A gap.
6. **ST 2110-41:2024 SSN literal-value conflict** — §6 prose + example use
   `SSN=ST2110-41:2024`; §9.2.2 IANA-registration prose uses
   `SSN=SMPTE2110-41:2024`. Phase 2 must decide which form the parser
   enforces.
7. **ST 2110-30 channel-count mismatch must be LENIENT** — when channel-order
   channel-count exceeds rtpmap channels, surplus channels are to be "treated
   as Undefined." A parser that rejects a mismatched count contradicts the
   SHALL.
8. **JPEG-XS §6.1.4 `fbblevel` bullet-binding trap** is confirmed at both
   TR-10-15-Part-1 §9 and IPMX-JPEG-XS-Profile v1.0 §6.1.4. The bullets
   (`transmode`, `packetmode`, `profile`, `level`, `sublevel`, `fbblevel`)
   attach to "shall populate the JPEG-XS Media Info Block… including:" — RTCP
   MIB fields, **not** SDP fmtp. The prior removal of the `fbblevel` SDP check
   (commit f6aa63f) is **validated** by this independent walk.
9. **Same bullet-binding shape exists in IPMX-PCM-Audio §6.1.4** — Sample
   rate / Sample size / Channel count / Packet time / Measured sample rate /
   Channel order bullets attach to a MIB-population clause, not an SDP one.
   If the parser has an audio fmtp check born from this misreading, it's a
   Direction-B finding.
10. **IPMX v1.0 profile clauses are thin** — every SDP-form definition
    delegates to TR-10-X. No IPMX-profile clause defines a new SDP attribute,
    a new fmtp parameter, or a new colorimetry / sampling / HDR value. The
    parser's IPMX-tier SDP validation should be a thin layer over its 2110
    validation — most of what IPMX "requires" lives in NMOS-Capabilities,
    RTCP-MIB, or device-capability territory.
11. **IPMX explicitly forbids whitelisting resolution / frame rate**. UV-07,
    UV-17, JX-08, and JX-20 in the IPMX Released v1.0 profiles all use
    "Undefined / Any" language — the parser must not impose a resolution or
    frame-rate whitelist at the IPMX tier.
12. **`a=group:FID` cross-stream uniqueness (RFC 5888 §3.1)** — each
    referenced `m=` must have a distinct (IP, port) transport address, using
    media-level `c=` if present, else session-level. Easy to miss.

---


# IETF — SDP base

## RFC 4566 (SDP, legacy base)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_rfc4566.md`_

# Audit Inventory: RFC 4566 — SDP: Session Description Protocol

| # | Spec | § | Verb | Verbatim quote | Summary | SDP? | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | RFC 4566 | 4.1 | SHOULD | "By default, this SHOULD be the remote address and remote port to which data is sent." | Default semantics: address/port = remote destination of data | Y | Recommendation, not strict; refers to c=/m= interpretation |
| 2 | RFC 4566 | 4.1 | NOT RECOMMENDED | "Some media types may redefine this behaviour, but this is NOT RECOMMENDED since it complicates implementations" | Discourages media types redefining address/port semantics | N | media type design guidance, not SDP-instance validation |
| 3 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "where <type> MUST be exactly one case-significant character and <value> is structured text whose format depends on <type>." | Each SDP line: type is exactly one case-significant char | Y | Core line-form rule |
| 4 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST NOT | "Whitespace MUST NOT be used on either side of the \"=\" sign." | No whitespace around `=` separator | Y | Line syntax |
| 5 | RFC 4566 | 5 | REQUIRED/OPTIONAL + MUST | "Some lines in each description are REQUIRED and some are OPTIONAL, but all MUST appear in exactly the order given here (the fixed order greatly enhances error detection and allows for a simple parser)." | Lines MUST appear in the fixed order specified | Y | Fundamental ordering rule; ordering listed v= o= s= i=* u=* e=* p=* c=* b=* t r=* z=* k=* a=* media... |
| 6 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "The set of type letters is deliberately small and not intended to be extensible -- an SDP parser MUST completely ignore any session description that contains a type letter that it does not understand." | Parser MUST ignore entire SDP description containing unknown type letter | Y | AMBIGUOUS: "completely ignore" — ignore-the-line vs. ignore-whole-description. Treat literally: whole SDP. Notes: AMBIGUOUS |
| 7 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "An SDP parser MUST ignore any attribute it doesn't understand." | Unknown attributes are ignored, not rejected | Y | parser behavior: cannot fail on unrecognised a= |
| 8 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MAY | "SDP field names and attribute names use only the US-ASCII subset of UTF-8, but textual fields and attribute values MAY use the full ISO 10646 character set." | Field names ASCII-only; textual values may use UTF-8 | Y | defined-value-set on names |
| 9 | RFC 4566 | 5 | SHOULD | "The sequence CRLF (0x0d0a) is used to end a record, although parsers SHOULD be tolerant and also accept records terminated with a single newline character." | CRLF terminates records; parser SHOULD accept LF too | Y | parser tolerance recommendation |
| 10 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "If the \"a=charset\" attribute is not present, these octet strings MUST be interpreted as containing ISO-10646 characters in UTF-8 encoding (the presence of the \"a=charset\" attribute may force some fields to be interpreted differently)." | Without a=charset, text fields are UTF-8 | Y | text field interpretation |
| 11 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "Any domain name used in SDP MUST comply with [1], [2]." | Domain names must comply with RFC 1034/1035 | Y | cross-ref: RFC 1034/1035 (DNS) |
| 12 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST | "Internationalised domain names (IDNs) MUST be represented using the ASCII Compatible Encoding (ACE) form defined in [11] and MUST NOT be directly represented in UTF-8 or any other encoding" | IDNs in SDP must use ACE form (xn--), not UTF-8 | Y | cross-ref: RFC 3490 (IDNA) |
| 13 | RFC 4566 | 5 | MUST NOT | "Internationalised domain names (IDNs) ... MUST NOT be directly represented in UTF-8 or any other encoding" | IDNs in SDP not directly UTF-8 | Y | paired with row 12 |
| 14 | RFC 4566 | 5.1 | defined-value-set | "v=0 ... This memo defines version 0.  There is no minor version number." | v= value is "0" | Y | only defined version |
| 15 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | MUST NOT | "The <username> MUST NOT contain spaces." | username (o= field 1) has no spaces | Y | o= sub-field constraint |
| 16 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | required-form | "<sess-id> is a numeric string such that the tuple of <username>, <sess-id>, <nettype>, <addrtype>, and <unicast-address> forms a globally unique identifier for the session." | sess-id is a numeric string | Y | defined-value-set: numeric (ABNF 1*DIGIT) |
| 17 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | required-form | "<sess-version> is a version number for this session description." | sess-version is numeric | Y | ABNF 1*DIGIT |
| 18 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | MAY | "Initially \"IN\" is defined to have the meaning \"Internet\", but other values MAY be registered in the future (see Section 8)." | nettype initial set: {IN}, extensible | Y | defined-value-set; IANA-registered |
| 19 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | MAY | "Initially \"IP4\" and \"IP6\" are defined, but other values MAY be registered in the future (see Section 8)." | addrtype initial set: {IP4, IP6}, extensible | Y | defined-value-set; IANA-registered |
| 20 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | SHOULD | "For both IP4 and IP6, the fully qualified domain name is the form that SHOULD be given unless this is unavailable, in which case the globally unique address MAY be substituted." | Prefer FQDN over IP literal in o= unicast-address | Y | recommendation |
| 21 | RFC 4566 | 5.2 | MUST NOT | "A local IP address MUST NOT be used in any context where the SDP description might leave the scope in which the address is meaningful (for example, a local address MUST NOT be included in an application-level referral that might leave the scope)." | Local IP forbidden in scope-leaving SDP | N | requires runtime knowledge of "leaves the scope"; not statically checkable from SDP |
| 22 | RFC 4566 | 5.3 | MUST | "There MUST be one and only one \"s=\" field per session description." | Exactly one s= per SDP | Y | required cardinality |
| 23 | RFC 4566 | 5.3 | MUST NOT | "The \"s=\" field MUST NOT be empty and SHOULD contain ISO 10646 characters (but see also the \"a=charset\" attribute)." | s= value non-empty | Y | required field non-empty (ABNF: text = byte-string = 1*) |
| 24 | RFC 4566 | 5.3 | SHOULD | "If a session has no meaningful name, the value \"s= \" SHOULD be used (i.e., a single space as the session name)." | If no name, use single space | Y | recommendation, also satisfies non-empty |
| 25 | RFC 4566 | 5.4 | MUST | "There MUST be at most one session-level \"i=\" field per session description, and at most one \"i=\" field per media." | At most one i= per session and per media | Y | cardinality |
| 26 | RFC 4566 | 5.4 | MUST | "If the \"a=charset\" attribute is not present, the \"i=\" field MUST contain ISO 10646 characters in UTF-8 encoding." | i= UTF-8 by default | Y | text encoding default |
| 27 | RFC 4566 | 5.5 | MUST | "This field is OPTIONAL, but if it is present it MUST be specified before the first media field." | u= must precede first m= | Y | ordering |
| 28 | RFC 4566 | 5.5 | cardinality | "No more than one URI field is allowed per session description." | At most one u= per SDP | Y | cardinality |
| 29 | RFC 4566 | 5.6 | MUST | "If an email address or phone number is present, it MUST be specified before the first media field." | e= / p= must precede first m= | Y | ordering |
| 30 | RFC 4566 | 5.6 | SHOULD | "Phone numbers SHOULD be given in the form of an international public telecommunication number (see ITU-T Recommendation E.164) preceded by a \"+\"." | p= preferred form: E.164 with + | Y | format recommendation; ABNF is more permissive |
| 31 | RFC 4566 | 5.6 | MUST | "Both email addresses and phone numbers can have an OPTIONAL free text string associated with them, normally giving the name of the person who may be contacted.  This MUST be enclosed in parentheses if it is present." | Optional name in e=/p= must be in parentheses | Y | AMBIGUOUS: the ABNF (§9) also permits the `dispname <addr>` form, which is also allowed in the prose ("alternative RFC 2822 [29] name quoting convention"). ABNF authoritative |
| 32 | RFC 4566 | 5.6 | SHOULD | "The free text string SHOULD be in the ISO-10646 character set with UTF-8 encoding, or alternatively in ISO-8859-1 or other encodings if the appropriate session-level \"a=charset\" attribute is set." | Free-text in e=/p= UTF-8 or per a=charset | Y | text encoding recommendation |
| 33 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST | "A session description MUST contain either at least one \"c=\" field in each media description or a single \"c=\" field at the session level." | c= required: session-level OR per-media | Y | structural requirement |
| 34 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MAY | "It MAY contain a single session-level \"c=\" field and additional \"c=\" field(s) per media description, in which case the per-media values override the session-level settings for the respective media." | Per-media c= overrides session-level c= | Y | layering rule |
| 35 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST | "Sessions using an IPv4 multicast connection address MUST also have a time to live (TTL) value present in addition to the multicast address." | IPv4 multicast c= must include TTL | Y | required form when condition met |
| 36 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST | "TTL values MUST be in the range 0-255." | TTL in [0,255] | Y | defined-value-set |
| 37 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST | "Although the TTL MUST be specified, its use to scope multicast traffic is deprecated; applications SHOULD use an administratively scoped address instead." | TTL is required for v4 mcast (restatement) | Y | duplicates row 35 |
| 38 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST NOT | "IPv6 multicast does not use TTL scoping, and hence the TTL value MUST NOT be present for IPv6 multicast." | IPv6 multicast c= must not include TTL | Y | required absence |
| 39 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MAY + MUST NOT | "Multiple addresses or \"c=\" lines MAY be specified on a per-media basis only if they provide multicast addresses for different layers in a hierarchical or layered encoding scheme.  They MUST NOT be specified for a session-level \"c=\" field." | Multiple c= or address-list only per media, only for layered mcast; session-level c= not allowed multiple | Y | constraint on c= cardinality |
| 40 | RFC 4566 | 5.7 | MUST NOT | "The slash notation for multiple addresses described above MUST NOT be used for IP unicast addresses." | No address-count slash on unicast c= | Y | forbids `addr/n` for unicast |
| 41 | RFC 4566 | 5.8 | SHOULD | "If the bandwidth of a session or media in a session is different from the bandwidth implicit from the scope, a \"b=CT:...\" line SHOULD be supplied for the session" | When scope-bandwidth differs, supply b=CT | Y | recommendation |
| 42 | RFC 4566 | 5.8 | NOT RECOMMENDED | "Use of the \"X-\" prefix is NOT RECOMMENDED: instead new modifiers SHOULD be registered with IANA in the standard namespace." | Avoid X- bwtype prefix | N | guidance only; validator silence per principle |
| 43 | RFC 4566 | 5.8 | MUST | "SDP parsers MUST ignore bandwidth fields with unknown modifiers." | Unknown bwtype: ignore the b= line, do not fail | Y | parser tolerance |
| 44 | RFC 4566 | 5.8 | MUST | "Modifiers MUST be alphanumeric and, although no length limit is given, it is recommended that they be short." | bwtype name alphanumeric (token in ABNF) | Y | defined-value-set (ABNF: bwtype = token, broader than alphanumeric — note conflict) AMBIGUOUS: prose says alphanumeric, ABNF says `token`. ABNF authoritative per audit rule 4 |
| 45 | RFC 4566 | 5.8 | MAY | "The <bandwidth> is interpreted as kilobits per second by default.  The definition of a new <bwtype> modifier MAY specify that the bandwidth is to be interpreted in some alternative unit (the \"CT\" and \"AS\" modifiers defined in this memo use the default units)." | Default units kbit/s; per-bwtype may differ | Y | unit semantics |
| 46 | RFC 4566 | 5.9 | MAY | "Multiple \"t=\" lines MAY be used if a session is active at multiple irregularly spaced times" | Multiple t= permitted | Y | cardinality permissive |
| 47 | RFC 4566 | 5.9 | required-form | "These values are the decimal representation of Network Time Protocol (NTP) time values in seconds since 1900" | t= sub-fields are NTP-seconds-since-1900 decimal | Y | format (ABNF: time = POS-DIGIT 9*DIGIT, or "0") |
| 48 | RFC 4566 | 5.9 | MUST | "SDP timestamps MUST continue counting seconds since 1900, NTP will use the value modulo the 64-bit limit" | SDP t= keeps counting past 2036, never wraps | Y | time format requirement |
| 49 | RFC 4566 | 5.9 | required-form | "If the <stop-time> is set to zero, then the session is not bounded ... If the <start-time> is also zero, the session is regarded as permanent." | stop=0 unbounded; start=stop=0 permanent | Y | defined semantics for "0" |
| 50 | RFC 4566 | 5.9 | SHOULD | "User interfaces SHOULD strongly discourage the creation of unbounded and permanent sessions" | UI recommendation, not SDP-form | N | UI behavior |
| 51 | RFC 4566 | 5.10 | required-form | "r=<repeat interval> <active duration> <offsets from start-time>" + "By default, all fields are in seconds" | r= fields: integer seconds or typed-time | Y | format; see ABNF |
| 52 | RFC 4566 | 5.10 | required-form | "The syntax for these is a number immediately followed by a single case-sensitive character.  Fractional units are not allowed -- a smaller unit should be used instead." | r= typed-time: integer + d|h|m|s; no fractions | Y | defined-value-set |
| 53 | RFC 4566 | 5.10 | defined-value-set | "The following unit specification characters are allowed: d - days (86400 seconds) / h - hours (3600 seconds) / m - minutes (60 seconds) / s - seconds (allowed for completeness)" | typed-time units: {d,h,m,s} | Y | defined-value-set; case-sensitive |
| 54 | RFC 4566 | 5.11 | required-form | "z=<adjustment time> <offset> <adjustment time> <offset> ...." | z= alternating adjustment time / offset pairs | Y | format |
| 55 | RFC 4566 | 5.12 | NOT RECOMMENDED | "A simple mechanism for key exchange is provided by the key field (\"k=\"), although this is primarily supported for compatibility with older implementations and its use is NOT RECOMMENDED." | k= deprecated/not recommended | Y | discouraged but allowed |
| 56 | RFC 4566 | 5.12 | MUST NOT | "k=clear:<encryption key>: This method MUST NOT be used unless it can be guaranteed that the SDP is conveyed over a secure channel." | k=clear: only on secure channel | N | requires runtime channel info |
| 57 | RFC 4566 | 5.12 | MUST NOT | "k=base64:<encoded encryption key>: This method MUST NOT be used unless it can be guaranteed that the SDP is conveyed over a secure channel." | k=base64: only on secure channel | N | requires runtime channel info |
| 58 | RFC 4566 | 5.12 | defined-value-set | "k=<method> / k=<method>:<encryption key>" with methods: clear, base64, uri, prompt | Defined k= methods: {clear, base64, uri, prompt} | Y | defined-value-set; ABNF authoritative |
| 59 | RFC 4566 | 5.12 | MUST NOT | "The key field MUST NOT be used unless it can be guaranteed that the SDP is conveyed over a secure and trusted channel." | k= field generally forbidden on untrusted transport | N | requires runtime channel info |
| 60 | RFC 4566 | 5.13 | MUST | "Attribute names MUST use the US-ASCII subset of ISO-10646/UTF-8." | a= attribute name (att-field) is US-ASCII | Y | name encoding (ABNF: att-field=token, ASCII-only) |
| 61 | RFC 4566 | 5.13 | MAY | "Attribute values are octet strings, and MAY use any octet value except 0x00 (Nul), 0x0A (LF), and 0x0D (CR)." | att-value bytes: not NUL/LF/CR | Y | byte-string constraint (ABNF: byte-string = 1*(%x01-09/%x0B-0C/%x0E-FF)) |
| 62 | RFC 4566 | 5.13 | MUST | "Attributes MUST be registered with IANA (see Section 8)." | New attributes must register with IANA | N | registry requirement, not per-SDP |
| 63 | RFC 4566 | 5.13 | MUST | "If an attribute is received that is not understood, it MUST be ignored by the receiver." | Unknown attribute: ignore (duplicate of §5) | Y | parser tolerance — already in row 7 |
| 64 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | defined-value-set | "<media> is the media type.  Currently defined media are \"audio\", \"video\", \"text\", \"application\", and \"message\", although this list may be extended in the future" | Initial media set: {audio,video,text,application,message}, extensible | Y | defined-value-set |
| 65 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | MUST | "If non-contiguous ports are used or if they don't follow the parity rule of even RTP ports and odd RTCP ports, the \"a=rtcp:\" attribute MUST be used." | a=rtcp: required when port scheme breaks parity | N | requires knowledge of actual RTP port use; SDP cannot statically detect "non-contiguous"; cross-ref: RFC 3605 |
| 66 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | MUST NOT | "Applications that are requested to send media to a <port> that is odd and where the \"a=rtcp:\" is present MUST NOT subtract 1 from the RTP port: that is, they MUST send the RTP to the port indicated in <port> and send the RTCP to the port indicated in the \"a=rtcp\" attribute." | Sender behavior: don't decrement odd RTP port | N | RTP sender behavior, not SDP form |
| 67 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | required-form | "m=<media> <port>/<number of ports> <proto> <fmt> ..." | m= port may carry /count for hierarchical | Y | format |
| 68 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | required-form | "<proto> is the transport protocol. ... The following transport protocols are defined ... udp ... RTP/AVP ... RTP/SAVP" | Initial proto set: {udp, RTP/AVP, RTP/SAVP}, extensible | Y | defined-value-set |
| 69 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | MAY + SHOULD | "When a list of payload type numbers is given, this implies that all of these payload formats MAY be used in the session, but the first of these formats SHOULD be used as the default format for the session." | First m= fmt is preferred default | Y | recommendation on first fmt PT |
| 70 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | SHOULD | "For dynamic payload type assignments the \"a=rtpmap:\" attribute (see Section 6) SHOULD be used to map from an RTP payload type number to a media encoding name that identifies the payload format." | Dynamic PT SHOULD have a=rtpmap | Y | recommendation (NB: §8.2.3 below upgrades this to MUST) |
| 71 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | MUST | "If the <proto> sub-field is \"udp\" the <fmt> sub-fields MUST reference a media type describing the format under the \"audio\", \"video\", \"text\", \"application\", or \"message\" top-level media types." | For proto=udp, fmt MUST be a media type under one of the 5 top-level types | Y | format constraint |
| 72 | RFC 4566 | 5.14 | MUST | "Rules for interpretation of the <fmt> sub-field MUST be defined when registering new protocols (see Section 8.2.2)." | New proto registrations must define fmt rules | N | registry requirement |
| 73 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=cat:<category> This attribute gives the dot-separated hierarchical category of the session." | a=cat: dot-separated category | Y | session-level attribute |
| 74 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=keywds:<keywords>" with session-level + charset-dependent | a=keywds value form | Y | session-level |
| 75 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=tool:<name and version of tool>" | a=tool value form | Y | session-level |
| 76 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=ptime:<packet time>  This gives the length of time in milliseconds represented by the media in a packet." | a=ptime: integer milliseconds | Y | media-level |
| 77 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHALL | "a=maxptime:<maximum packet time> This gives the maximum amount of media that can be encapsulated in each packet, expressed as time in milliseconds.  The time SHALL be calculated as the sum of the time the media present in the packet represents." | maxptime calculation = sum of media time | N | calculation rule for senders, not an SDP form-check |
| 78 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=rtpmap:<payload type> <encoding name>/<clock rate> [/<encoding parameters>]" | a=rtpmap value form: PT SP name/rate[/params] | Y | media-level |
| 79 | RFC 4566 | 6 | MUST | "RTP profiles that specify the use of dynamic payload types MUST define the set of valid encoding names and/or a means to register encoding names if that profile is to be used with SDP." | Profile registration requirement | N | profile spec requirement, not SDP-instance |
| 80 | RFC 4566 | 6 | defined-form | "For audio streams, <encoding parameters> indicates the number of audio channels.  This parameter is OPTIONAL and may be omitted if the number of channels is one, provided that no additional parameters are needed." | rtpmap audio encoding-params = channels; optional default 1 | Y | format semantic per media type |
| 81 | RFC 4566 | 6 | defined-form | "For video streams, no encoding parameters are currently specified." | rtpmap video encoding-params not defined | Y | format semantic per media type |
| 82 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD NOT | "Additional encoding parameters MAY be defined in the future, but codec-specific parameters SHOULD NOT be added.  Parameters added to an \"a=rtpmap:\" attribute SHOULD only be those required for a session directory to make the choice of appropriate media to participate in a session." | rtpmap params not codec-specific | N | spec-design guidance for future params |
| 83 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD | "Note that recvonly applies to the media only, not to any associated control protocol (e.g., an RTP-based system in recvonly mode SHOULD still send RTCP packets)." | recvonly: RTCP still sent | N | RTP/RTCP behavior |
| 84 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD | "If none of the attributes \"sendonly\", \"recvonly\", \"inactive\", and \"sendrecv\" is present, \"sendrecv\" SHOULD be assumed as the default for sessions that are not of the conference type \"broadcast\" or \"H332\" (see below)." | Default direction = sendrecv (unless broadcast/H332) | Y | implicit-value rule for consumers |
| 85 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD | "Note that sendonly applies only to the media, and any associated control protocol (e.g., RTCP) SHOULD still be received and processed as normal." | sendonly: RTCP still received | N | RTP/RTCP behavior |
| 86 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD | "Note that an RTP-based system SHOULD still send RTCP, even if started inactive." | inactive: RTCP still sent | N | RTP/RTCP behavior |
| 87 | RFC 4566 | 6 | defined-value-set | "a=orient:<orientation> ... Permitted values are \"portrait\", \"landscape\", and \"seascape\" (upside-down landscape)." | a=orient value set: {portrait, landscape, seascape} | Y | defined-value-set |
| 88 | RFC 4566 | 6 | defined-value-set | "a=type:<conference type> ... Suggested values are \"broadcast\", \"meeting\", \"moderated\", \"test\", and \"H332\"." | a=type suggested set: {broadcast,meeting,moderated,test,H332} | Y | AMBIGUOUS: "Suggested values" — not a closed set; cannot reject unknown |
| 89 | RFC 4566 | 6 | MUST | "The charset specified MUST be one of those registered with IANA, such as ISO-8859-1." | a=charset: IANA-registered charset name | Y | defined-value-set (IANA charset registry) |
| 90 | RFC 4566 | 6 | MUST | "The character set identifier is a US-ASCII string and MUST be compared against the IANA identifiers using a case-insensitive comparison." | a=charset comparison case-insensitive | Y | comparison rule |
| 91 | RFC 4566 | 6 | SHOULD | "If the identifier is not recognised or not supported, all strings that are affected by it SHOULD be regarded as octet strings." | Unknown charset: treat as octets | Y | tolerance rule |
| 92 | RFC 4566 | 6 | MUST | "Note that a character set specified MUST still prohibit the use of bytes 0x00 (Nul), 0x0A (LF), and 0x0d (CR)." | Even non-default charset: no NUL/LF/CR | Y | global byte exclusion |
| 93 | RFC 4566 | 6 | MUST | "Character sets requiring the use of these characters MUST define a quoting mechanism that prevents these bytes from appearing within text fields." | Charset registrations with reserved bytes: must define quoting | N | charset-spec design requirement |
| 94 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "The \"sdplang\" attribute value must be a single RFC 3066 language tag in US-ASCII [9]." | a=sdplang value: single RFC 3066 tag in ASCII | Y | defined-value-set; cross-ref: RFC 3066/5646 |
| 95 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "The \"lang\" attribute value must be a single RFC 3066 language tag in US-ASCII [9]." | a=lang value: single RFC 3066 tag in ASCII | Y | defined-value-set; cross-ref: RFC 3066/5646 |
| 96 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=framerate:<frame rate> This gives the maximum video frame rate in frames/sec.  Decimal representations of fractional values using the notation \"<integer>.<fraction>\" are allowed.  It is a media-level attribute, defined only for video media" | a=framerate: integer or integer.fraction; video only | Y | format; "video only" is meta-constraint |
| 97 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=quality:<quality> ... an integer value. ... For video, the value is in the range 0 to 10" | a=quality: integer | Y | defined-value-set (integer; range 0-10 only stated for video as "following suggested meaning") |
| 98 | RFC 4566 | 6 | required-form | "a=fmtp:<format> <format specific parameters> ... The format must be one of the formats specified for the media." | a=fmtp format token must match an m= fmt | Y | cross-line consistency |
| 99 | RFC 4566 | 6 | cardinality | "At most one instance of this attribute is allowed for each format." | At most one a=fmtp per fmt per media | Y | cardinality |
| 100 | RFC 4566 | 6 | table-derived | Attribute level table: cat/keywds/tool/type/charset = Session; ptime/maxptime/rtpmap/orient/framerate/quality/fmtp = Media; recvonly/sendrecv/sendonly/inactive/sdplang/lang = Either | Per-attribute placement scope (session/media/either) | Y | scope constraint per attribute |
| 101 | RFC 4566 | 6 | table-derived | Charset-dependent column: only keywds = Yes; all others = No | Per-attribute charset dependency | Y | value-interpretation rule |
| 102 | RFC 4566 | 7 | MUST NOT | "Software that parses a session description MUST NOT be able to start other software except that which is specifically configured as appropriate software to participate in multimedia sessions." | Parser security: no arbitrary process spawning | N | implementation security policy |
| 103 | RFC 4566 | 7 | MUST NOT | "Thus, a session description arriving by session announcement, email, session invitation, or WWW page MUST NOT deliver the user into an interactive multimedia session unless the user has explicitly pre-authorised such action." | No silent autojoin | N | application security policy |
| 104 | RFC 4566 | 7 | MUST NOT | "SDP MUST NOT be used to convey key material, unless it can be guaranteed that the channel over which the SDP is delivered is both private and authenticated." | k= only on private+authenticated channel | N | transport-context check |
| 105 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.1 | MUST | "For media other than existing top-level media content types, a Standards Track RFC MUST be produced for a new top-level content type to be registered, and the registration MUST provide good justification why no existing media name is appropriate" | New media name: requires Standards Track RFC | N | registry policy |
| 106 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.1 | MUST | "If these media types are considered useful in the future, a Standards Track RFC MUST be produced to document their use.  Until that is done, applications SHOULD NOT use these types and SHOULD NOT declare support for them in SIP capabilities declarations (even though they exist in the registry created by RFC 3840)." | "control", "data" media: not to be used until re-specified | Y | recommendation against (SHOULD NOT) |

| 110 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.3 | MUST | "If the payload type number is dynamically assigned by this session description, an additional \"rtpmap\" attribute MUST be included to specify the format name and parameters as defined by the media type registration for the payload format." | Dynamic PT → a=rtpmap REQUIRED (stronger than §5.14's SHOULD) | Y | scope: "RTP payload formats under the \"RTP/AVP\" and \"RTP/SAVP\" profiles MUST use the payload type number as their \"fmt\" value." — dynamic-PT rule is part of §8.2.3 and binds to RTP/AVP, RTP/SAVP. | 111 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.3 | MUST | "Registrations of new formats MUST specify which transport protocols they apply to." | fmt registration scope explicit | N | registry policy |
| 112 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.4 | MUST | "Attribute field names (\"att-field\") MUST be registered with IANA and documented, because of noticeable issues due to conflicting attributes under the same name." | att-field MUST be IANA-registered | N | registry policy (parser MUST still ignore unknowns per §5.13/§5) |
| 113 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.5 | MUST | "New bandwidth specifiers (\"bwtype\" fields) MUST be registered with IANA." | bwtype must be registered | N | registry policy |
| 114 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.6 | MUST | "A new network type registration MUST reference an RFC that gives details of the network type and address type and specifies how and when they would be used." | nettype registration cites RFC | N | registry policy |

| 116 | RFC 4566 | 8.2.7 | MUST | "A new address type registration MUST reference an RFC giving details of the syntax of the address type." | addrtype registration cites RFC | N | registry policy |

| 118 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `session-description = proto-version origin-field session-name-field information-field uri-field email-fields phone-fields connection-field bandwidth-fields time-fields key-field attribute-fields media-descriptions` | Top-level session order (authoritative ABNF) | Y | authoritative ordering; matches §5 list |
| 119 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `proto-version = %x76 "=" 1*DIGIT CRLF ;this memo describes version 0` | v= ABNF: digit sequence (any value valid grammatically) | Y | ABNF allows 1*DIGIT but §5.1 fixes value to 0. | 127 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `bandwidth-fields = *(%x62 "=" bwtype ":" bandwidth CRLF)` | b= ABNF: 0..N, colon-separator | Y | authoritative |

| 129 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `repeat-fields = %x72 "=" repeat-interval SP typed-time 1*(SP typed-time)` | r= ABNF: interval + duration + 1..N offsets | Y | authoritative; minimum 3 typed values total |
| 130 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `zone-adjustments = %x7a "=" time SP ["-"] typed-time *(SP time SP ["-"] typed-time)` | z= ABNF: 1..N (time, signed-typed-time) pairs | Y | authoritative |
| 131 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `key-field = [%x6b "=" key-type CRLF]` and `key-type = "prompt" / "clear:" text / "base64:" base64 / "uri:" uri` | k= ABNF: optional; method ∈ {prompt, clear:, base64:, uri:} | Y | authoritative closed value set |
| 132 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `attribute-fields = *(%x61 "=" attribute CRLF)` and `attribute = (att-field ":" att-value) / att-field` | a= ABNF: 0..N; flag or key:value | Y | authoritative |
| 133 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `media-descriptions = *( media-field information-field *connection-field bandwidth-fields key-field attribute-fields )` and `media-field = %x6d "=" media SP port ["/" integer] SP proto 1*(SP fmt) CRLF` | m= section ABNF: required order i= c=* b= k= a= ; m= form: media SP port[/n] SP proto SP fmt+ | Y | authoritative; "*connection-field" allows multiple c= per media (per row 39) |

| 136 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `sess-version = 1*DIGIT` | sess-version: 1 or more digits | Y | authoritative |

| 144 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `repeat-interval = POS-DIGIT *DIGIT [fixed-len-time-unit]` and `typed-time = 1*DIGIT [fixed-len-time-unit]` | r= values: integer or integer + unit char | Y | authoritative |

| 147 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `att-field = token` and `att-value = byte-string` | a= ABNF: name=token; value=byte-string | Y | authoritative |
| 148 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `media = token` | m= 1st field: token | Y | authoritative |
| 149 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `fmt = token` | m= fmt: token (not bare integer; tokens include digits) | Y | authoritative |
| 150 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `proto = token *("/" token)` | m= proto: token(s) separated by `/` | Y | authoritative |
| 151 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `port = 1*DIGIT` | m= port: digits | Y | authoritative; no upper bound stated in ABNF |
| 152 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `unicast-address = IP4-address / IP6-address / FQDN / extn-addr` | unicast-address forms | Y | authoritative |
| 153 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `multicast-address = IP4-multicast / IP6-multicast / FQDN / extn-addr` | multicast-address forms | Y | authoritative |
| 154 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `IP4-multicast = m1 3( "." decimal-uchar ) "/" ttl [ "/" integer ] ; IPv4 multicast addresses may be in the range 224.0.0.0 to 239.255.255.255` and `m1 = ("22" ("4"/"5"/"6"/"7"/"8"/"9")) / ("23" DIGIT )` | IPv4 multicast: first octet 224-239; TTL mandatory; optional address count | Y | authoritative — note `/ ttl` is non-optional in ABNF, matching row 35 |
| 155 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `IP6-multicast = hexpart [ "/" integer ] ; IPv6 address starting with FF` | IPv6 multicast: FF-prefix; optional address count; NO ttl slot | Y | authoritative — no `/ttl` syntactically (reinforces row 38) |
| 156 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `ttl = (POS-DIGIT *2DIGIT) / "0"` | TTL: "0" or 1..3 digits starting non-zero (i.e. 1..999 syntactically) | Y | authoritative; §5.7 prose narrows to 0-255 |
| 157 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `FQDN = 4*(alpha-numeric / "-" / ".") ; fully qualified domain name as specified in RFC 1035 (and updates)` | FQDN: 4+ chars from alphanum, `-`, `.` | Y | authoritative |
| 158 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `IP4-address = b1 3("." decimal-uchar)` and `b1 = decimal-uchar ; less than "224"` | IPv4 unicast: first octet < 224 (i.e. not multicast/reserved) | Y | authoritative; reinforces unicast vs multicast distinction at ABNF level |
| 159 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `IP6-address = hexpart [ ":" IP4-address ]` etc. | IPv6 unicast/general form per RFC 2373 App.B | Y | authoritative; cross-ref: RFC 2373 |
| 160 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `extn-addr = non-ws-string` | extn-addr (for non-IP nettype): visible chars no space | Y | authoritative |
| 161 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `text = byte-string` and `byte-string = 1*(%x01-09/%x0B-0C/%x0E-FF) ;any byte except NUL, CR, or LF` | text: 1+ bytes, no NUL/LF/CR | Y | authoritative — note minimum 1 byte (reinforces non-empty for s=) |
| 162 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `non-ws-string = 1*(VCHAR/%x80-FF) ;string of visible characters` | non-ws-string: visible chars including UTF-8 high bytes | Y | authoritative |
| 163 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `token-char = %x21 / %x23-27 / %x2A-2B / %x2D-2E / %x30-39 / %x41-5A / %x5E-7E` and `token = 1*(token-char)` | token: specific allowed printable byte set, no `"`, `(`, `)`, `,`, `/`, `:`, `;`, `<`, `=`, `>`, `?`, `@`, `[`, `\`, `]` | Y | authoritative — precise character class |
| 164 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `email-safe = %x01-09/%x0B-0C/%x0E-27/%x2A-3B/%x3D/%x3F-FF ;any byte except NUL, CR, LF, or the quoting characters ()<>` | email-safe: bytes for free-text in e=/p= name | Y | authoritative |
| 165 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `integer = POS-DIGIT *DIGIT` | integer: leading non-zero digit | Y | authoritative — no leading zeros |
| 166 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `decimal-uchar` rule: range 0-255 | IPv4 octet = decimal-uchar = 0..255 | Y | authoritative |
| 167 | RFC 4566 | 9 | ABNF | `POS-DIGIT = %x31-39 ; 1 - 9` | POS-DIGIT: 1-9 | Y | authoritative primitive |

## Summary

- Total clauses enumerated: 167
- SDP-constraining (Y): 138
- AMBIGUOUS count: 7 (rows 6, 31, 44, 88, 110, 119, plus the §5.14 vs §8.2.3 dynamic-PT SHOULD↔MUST conflict captured in row 110)

## Anomalies

1. Row 6 (§5 "MUST completely ignore any session description"): the literal reading is to discard the entire SDP on encountering an unknown type letter, which conflicts with how the rest of the spec handles forward extension (parser tolerance, e.g. row 7 / row 43). Flagged AMBIGUOUS for main-thread interpretation.
2. Row 44 / §5.8 prose ("Modifiers MUST be alphanumeric") vs §9 ABNF (`bwtype = token`) — direct conflict. Per audit rule 4, ABNF authoritative. The parser should accept `token` for bwtype, not just alphanumeric.
3. Row 88 / §6 a=type "Suggested values" — the spec uses "suggested," not normative; the value list is NOT closed, so a validator cannot reject unknown `a=type` values.
4. Row 110 / §8.2.3 promotes the §5.14 SHOULD ("Dynamic PT → a=rtpmap") to a MUST when the proto is RTP/AVP or RTP/SAVP. Effectively dynamic PT in those profiles requires rtpmap. Bullet-binding-sensitive: the MUST is part of §8.2.3's "RTP payload formats under the \"RTP/AVP\" and \"RTP/SAVP\" profiles MUST use the payload type number as their \"fmt\" value" paragraph; the dynamic-PT MUST is its second sentence.
5. Row 119 / §9 ABNF `proto-version = %x76 "=" 1*DIGIT CRLF` allows ANY digit string, but §5.1 prose fixes the value to `0`. ABNF authoritative — but `v=0` is the only normatively meaningful value in this memo.
6. Row 156: ABNF `ttl = (POS-DIGIT *2DIGIT) / "0"` syntactically permits up to 999, but §5.7 prose says "TTL values MUST be in the range 0-255." Prose MUST is unambiguous and tighter; should be applied. Not flagged AMBIGUOUS — the prose is normative MUST.
7. Row 165: ABNF `integer = POS-DIGIT *DIGIT` rejects leading zeros for any field typed as `integer` (notably the `[/n]` address-count after IP4-multicast TTL, the optional `[/integer]` in m= port count, and `<offset>` in z= which is typed-time). Parser must reject "01", "00" in these positions.
8. Spec uses MUST/MUST NOT/SHOULD/SHOULD NOT/MAY/REQUIRED/OPTIONAL and never uses SHALL/SHALL NOT in §5-§9 normative text. §6 a=maxptime contains the only "SHALL" in the body of the spec (row 77) — and that "SHALL" describes a packet-construction calculation, not an SDP form-check.
9. Section 10 ("Summary of Changes from RFC 2327"): explicitly notes "Most uses of the \"x-\" prefix notation for experimental parameters are disallowed and the other uses are deprecated." This re-emphasises row 42 / §5.8.

---

## RFC 8866 (SDP, current)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_rfc8866.md`_

# Audit Inventory — RFC 8866 (SDP: Session Description Protocol)

Spec under walk: RFC 8866 (January 2021), obsoletes RFC 4566.
Source: https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8866.txt (read directly, full text).

| # | Spec | § | Verb | Verbatim quote | Summary | SDP? | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST | "An SDP description MUST conform to the syntax defined in Section 9." | Whole description must match the §9 ABNF | Y | delta-from-4566: clarification — ties strictness explicitly to ABNF |
| 2 | RFC 8866 | 5 | "must appear in exactly" | "Some lines in each description are required and some are optional, but when present, they must appear in exactly the order given here." | Required field order is mandatory (v/o/s/i/u/e/p/c/b/t/r/z/k/a, then media) | Y | delta-from-4566: silent (same rule, reworded). Note: lower-case "must" — but ABNF in §9 makes the order normative. |
| 3 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST | "an SDP parser MUST completely ignore or reject any session description that contains a type letter that it does not understand." | Unknown <type>= line letters must be ignored or rejected | Y | delta-from-4566: clarification (4566 said "ignore"; 8866 adds "or reject") |
| 4 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST | "An SDP parser MUST ignore any attribute it doesn't understand." | Unknown a= attributes must be ignored | Y | delta-from-4566: silent |
| 5 | RFC 8866 | 5 | "MUST be interpreted as" | "If the \"a=charset:\" attribute is not present, these octet strings MUST be interpreted as containing ISO-10646 characters in UTF-8 encoding." | Default charset for s= / i= text is UTF-8 | Y | delta-from-4566: silent |
| 6 | RFC 8866 | 5 | "any octet with the exceptions of" | "Text-containing fields such as the session-name-field and information-field are octet strings that may contain any octet with the exceptions of 0x00 (Nul), 0x0a (ASCII newline), and 0x0d (ASCII carriage return)." | Text fields exclude NUL/CR/LF | Y | defined-value-set; matches byte-string ABNF |
| 7 | RFC 8866 | 5 | SHOULD | "The sequence CRLF (0x0d0a) is used to end a line, although parsers SHOULD be tolerant and also accept lines terminated with a single newline character." | CRLF is the canonical line terminator; parsers SHOULD also accept LF | Y | delta-from-4566: clarification (4566 was effectively "MUST CRLF" but real-world LF acceptance now blessed). AMBIGUOUS: SHOULD-tolerance — accept-or-reject is implementation choice |
| 8 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST | "Any domain name used in SDP MUST comply with [RFC1034] and [RFC1035]." | Domain names in o=, u=, e=, c=, a= must be RFC 1034/1035 compliant | Y | delta-from-4566: clarification |
| 9 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST | "Internationalized domain names (IDNs) MUST be represented using the ASCII Compatible Encoding (ACE) form defined in [RFC5890]" | IDNs must use ACE form | Y | delta-from-4566: refinement (4566 silent on IDN); IDNs in raw UTF-8 are forbidden |
| 10 | RFC 8866 | 5 | MUST NOT | "and MUST NOT be directly represented in UTF-8 or any other encoding" | IDNs must not be raw UTF-8 in SDP | Y | delta-from-4566: new — same clause as #9 |
