| 28 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §6.5 | shall not | "Senders conforming to the CTM shall not transmit RTP packets earlier than one frame period before the requirement above." | CTM earliest-transmit bound. | N | RTP transmit timing; not SDP. |
| 29 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §6.5 | shall | "All Receivers shall be able to receive CTM streams." | All receivers shall receive CTM. | N | Receiver capability; not SDP-signaled. |
| 30 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "The SDP object shall be constructed as described in IETF RFC 8331, subject also to the provisions of SMPTE ST 2110-10." | SDP must follow RFC 8331 + ST 2110-10. | Y | Top-level reference: SDP construction governed by RFC 8331 (e.g. m=video, rtpmap smpte291/90000, fmtp parameters) and ST 2110-10 provisions. |
| 31 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall not | "Section 4.1 of IETF RFC 8331 permits the use of Flow Identification ("FID") semantics to group streams within the SDP; such use is inconsistent with the "one SDP object per RTP Stream" provision of SMPTE ST 2110-10 and therefore Flow Identification ("FID") semantics shall not be used under this standard." | `a=group:FID` shall not be used. | Y | **Explicit SDP prohibition**: `a=group:FID` is forbidden for streams conforming to ST 2110-40. Cite: ST 2110-40:2023 §7. (Note: scope is "streams under this standard," not all SDPs.) |
| 32 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "Senders implementing this standard shall signal a Format Specific Parameter SSN with the value ST2110-40:2018 unless they are signaling Format Specific Parameter TM, in which case they shall signal the value ST2110-40:2023." | SSN fmtp parameter is required; value depends on whether TM is signaled. | Y | **Required fmtp param `SSN`** with defined values `ST2110-40:2018` or `ST2110-40:2023` (conditional on TM presence). |
| 33 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "Receivers shall consider a Format Specific Parameter SSN value of ST2110-40:2021 as equivalent to a value of ST2110-40:2023." | Receiver-side equivalence: SSN=ST2110-40:2021 ≡ SSN=ST2110-40:2023. | Y (defined-value) | Adds `ST2110-40:2021` to the defined SSN value set as an alias. Receivers must accept it; a validator should not reject an SDP with `SSN=ST2110-40:2021`. |
| 34 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "Senders implementing the Low-Latency Transmission Model shall signal a Format Specific Parameter TM with the value LLTM in the SDP." | LLTM senders signal `TM=LLTM`. | Y | **Defined fmtp value**: TM=LLTM (conditional on transmission model). |
| 35 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | may | "Senders implementing the Compatible Transmission Model may signal a Format Specific Parameter TM with the value CTM in the SDP." | CTM senders may signal `TM=CTM`. | Y | Optional fmtp param TM with defined value CTM. Defined value set for TM = {LLTM, CTM}. |
| 36 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | should | "If a Format Specific Parameter TM is not present in the SDP, Receivers should assume the value CTM." | Default TM=CTM. | Y | Receiver-side default; informs that TM absence implies CTM. Not a sender-side requirement. |
| 37 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "All Senders shall signal the Format Specific Parameter exactframerate as defined in SMPTE ST 2110-20:2022 Clause 7.2 to indicate the frame rate related to the ANC data in the stream." | **Required fmtp param `exactframerate`** in every ANC SDP. | Y | **Required fmtp param** `exactframerate` for all senders. Definition borrowed from ST 2110-20:2022 §7.2 (cross-reference). Implication: an SDP for smpte291 with no exactframerate fmtp parameter is non-conformant. |
| 38 | ST 2110-40:2023 | §7 | shall | "If a Sender is operating with a value of TROFFSETANC that is different than the default value TRODEFAULT for the prevailing video format, then the Format Specific Parameter TROFF shall be signaled using the same definition as SMPTE ST 2110-21." | Conditional: TROFF fmtp required when non-default. | Y | **Conditional fmtp param `TROFF`** — required if non-default offset; otherwise optional. Definition per ST 2110-21. |

---

**Counts**:
- **Total normative clauses enumerated**: 38
- **SDP-constraining (Y or indirect)**: 11 (rows 7, 8, 13, 22, 30, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 37, 38) — note row 22 is indirect via TROFF, row 8 is "need not" (permissive), row 36 is receiver-side. Strict count of **prohibitions/required SDP forms a validator can enforce against an SDP**: 7 (rows 13, 31, 32, 34, 35, 37, 38, plus the defined-value rows 8 and 33).
- **AMBIGUOUS**: 1 (row 7 — required SDP fmtp conditional on RTP payload behavior not visible in SDP alone)
- **N (out of SDP scope)**: 23

---

## Key observations

1. **Spec is short and SDP-focused in §7.** ST 2110-40:2023 packs all SDP requirements into §7 (one page of normative text). The rest of the document is RTP payload mapping (§5), receiver SDI-construction guidance (§5.2.3), and transmit timing models (§6).

2. **Explicit SDP prohibitions** (validator can enforce against SDP text):
   - **`a=group:FID` is forbidden** for streams conforming to ST 2110-40 (§7, row 31). This is the only outright SDP prohibition.

3. **Required SDP fmtp parameters** for every conformant ST 2110-40 sender:
   - **`SSN`** (row 32) — defined values `ST2110-40:2018`, `ST2110-40:2023`, with `ST2110-40:2021` accepted as equivalent on the receive side (row 33). Sender selection of value is **conditional** on whether `TM` is signaled.
   - **`exactframerate`** (row 37) — definition borrowed from ST 2110-20:2022 §7.2. Required for **all** senders.

4. **Conditional SDP fmtp parameters**:
   - **`TM`** (rows 34, 35) — required value `LLTM` for LLTM senders; optional value `CTM` for CTM senders. Defined value set: {`LLTM`, `CTM`}. Absence implies CTM (row 36, receiver-side default).
   - **`TROFF`** (row 38) — required when sender's TROFFSETANC differs from default; definition per ST 2110-21.
   - **`VPID_Code`** (row 7, 8) — required from senders proposing exact SDI line/stream locations (not Line_Number = 0x7FE or 0x7FF). Other senders **need not** signal it (row 8 = explicit permission to omit). **AMBIGUOUS for SDP-only validation**: a validator cannot tell from SDP alone whether the sender is proposing exact location, so VPID_Code presence cannot be required from SDP text alone. Best the validator can do: if VPID_Code is present, validate it against the RFC 8331 defined value set.

5. **rtpmap requirement (implicit, defined-value)**:
   - **Clock rate = 90 kHz** (row 13). This constrains `a=rtpmap:<PT> smpte291/90000`. The rtpmap encoding name `smpte291` and the rate `90000` come from RFC 8331; ST 2110-40 §5.3 reiterates the 90 kHz rate.

6. **No m= line direct mandate.** ST 2110-40:2023 does **not** explicitly mandate `m=video` for ANC streams — it defers to RFC 8331 (row 30) for the SDP construction. RFC 8331 is the authority for the m= line type for smpte291 streams. (Validator should consult RFC 8331 inventory for the m= line requirement.)

7. **No FEC / DUP / 2022-7 statements.** ST 2110-40:2023 says nothing direct about `a=group:DUP` or redundancy. Only `a=group:FID` is prohibited.

8. **No mediaclk / ts-refclk statements.** ST 2110-40:2023 defers RTP Clock Offset to ST 2110-10 (row 14). Validator should look at ST 2110-10 §6.3.1 / §6.3.2 for mediaclk and ts-refclk requirements that would apply to an ANC stream.

9. **Bullet-binding risk**: none observed. §7's normative content is in prose paragraphs, not bullets. Each shall/may/should is a complete sentence with clear scope.

10. **What changed vs. 2018**: the 2023 revision added §6.4 (Low-Latency Transmission Model), §6.5 (Compatible Transmission Model), and the SDP signaling for them (`TM`, the conditional SSN value). The 2018 version had `SSN=ST2110-40:2018` only, no TM parameter, and effectively only the CTM model. Validators that target ST 2110-40:2018 should accept `SSN=ST2110-40:2018` without TM; validators that target 2023 should accept either `SSN=ST2110-40:2018` (no TM) or `SSN=ST2110-40:2023` + TM, plus the 2021-equivalent alias.

11. **`exactframerate` cross-reference**: ST 2110-40 borrows `exactframerate` syntax/semantics from ST 2110-20:2022 §7.2. A validator should reuse the same parser/validator for exactframerate as used for ST 2110-20 video.

12. **`TROFF` cross-reference**: TROFF for ANC follows ST 2110-21's definition. Same parser/validator as for ST 2110-21 video TROFF.

---

## SMPTE ST 2110-41:2024 (Fast Metadata)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_st2110-41.md`_

# SMPTE ST 2110-41:2024 Normative Clause Inventory

**Spec**: SMPTE ST 2110-41:2024 — Professional Media over Managed IP Networks: Fast Metadata Framework
**Source**: `/Users/andrewstarks/Library/CloudStorage/Dropbox/Personal/Claude/Macnica/Standards Related/smpte_standards_internal/st2110-41-2024.md`
**Audit scope**: Phase 1 enumeration only — no comparison against parser.

| # | Spec | § | Verb | Verbatim quote | Summary | SDP? | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | ST 2110-41 | 2 | defined-meaning | "The keyword \"reserved\" indicates a provision that is not defined at this time, shall not be used, and may be defined in the future. The keyword \"forbidden\" indicates \"reserved\" and in addition indicates that the provision will never be defined in the future." | "reserved" = not used; "forbidden" = will never be defined. | N | Conformance terminology only; no SDP impact. |
| 2 | ST 2110-41 | 2 | SHALL | "Unless otherwise specified, the order of precedence of the types of normative information in this document shall be as follows: Normative prose shall be the authoritative definition; tables shall be next; then formal languages; then figures; and then any other language forms." | Order of normative precedence within this document. | N | Document precedence rule; not SDP. |
| 3 | ST 2110-41 | 5.1 | SHALL | "Each RTP packet shall contain zero or more Data Item Packages." | RTP payload may be empty or contain ≥1 Data Item Package. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 4 | ST 2110-41 | 5.1 | SHALL | "Even if no Data Item Packages are transmitted, Senders shall transmit at least one RTP packet every 500 ms in order to allow for detection of transport loss." | Sender keep-alive: ≥1 RTP packet per 500 ms. | N | Sender transmission timing; runtime behavior, not SDP signaling. |
| 5 | ST 2110-41 | 5.1 | SHALL | "RTP Streams compliant to this specification shall be compliant with the provisions of SMPTE ST 2110-10." | -41 streams inherit ST 2110-10 conformance. | Y | Cross-spec inheritance: ST 2110-10 SDP rules apply (incl. ts-refclk, mediaclk, ptime considerations from -10 §6). |
| 6 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The fields of the RTP packet header and their order shall be as defined in IETF RFC 3550." | RTP header fields and order per RFC 3550. | N | RTP packet structure; not SDP. |
| 7 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The Payload Type field shall refer to a dynamically allocated payload type chosen in the range of 96 through 127. The dynamically allocated value shall be signaled in the SDP in accordance with IETF RFC 4566." | PT = dynamic 96–127, signaled in SDP per RFC 4566. | Y | SDP: media-level PT in `m=application <port> RTP/AVP <PT>` and `a=rtpmap:<PT> …` must be in 96–127. |
| 8 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The Timestamp field shall contain the RTP Timestamp as specified in this specification." | RTP Timestamp per §5.3. | N | RTP packet header rule; not SDP. |
| 9 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The SSRC field shall be as specified in IETF RFC 3550." | SSRC per RFC 3550. | N | RTP packet header rule; not SDP. |
| 10 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The marker bit shall be set to 0 for all packets." | M-bit fixed to 0. | N | RTP packet header rule; not SDP. |
| 11 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "The RTP header sequence number field shall contain a 16-bit packet sequence counter." | Sequence-number field semantics. | N | RTP packet header rule; not SDP. |
| 12 | ST 2110-41 | 5.2 | SHALL | "Any header extensions shall be compliant with IETF RFC 8285." | RTP header extensions follow RFC 8285. | N | RTP packet header rule; not SDP. |
| 13 | ST 2110-41 | 5.3 | SHALL | "In all cases, the RTP Clock rate shall be signaled in the SDP as specified in IETF RFC 4566." | RTP Clock rate signaled in SDP (rtpmap rate field) per RFC 4566. | Y | SDP: `a=rtpmap:<PT> <encoding-name>/<rate>` — the rate token is required and must reflect the RTP clock rate defined by the Data Item document. The clock rate value itself is set by the Data Item document, not by -41. |
| 14 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "The RTP Payload shall consist of a sequence of zero or more Data Item Packages." | RTP payload = zero+ Data Item Packages. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 15 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "Each Data Item Package shall be completely contained with the RTP Payload of a single RTP Packet (no partial Data Item Packages)." | No fragmentation of a single Data Item Package across packets. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 16 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "The total length of the UDP packet that encompasses each RTP Packet shall be less than or equal to the Standard UDP Size Limit defined in SMPTE ST 2110-10." | UDP packet ≤ ST 2110-10 Standard UDP Size Limit. | N | Transmission constraint; defined by ST 2110-10. Not SDP signaling. |
| 17 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "Each Data Item Package shall contain a Data Item Type, Data Item K-bit, and Data Item Length field, followed by one or more 32-bit Data Item Contents elements." | Data Item Package structure: Type + K + Length + ≥1 Contents word. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 18 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "The Data Item Type field shall signal the Data Item Type corresponding to the contents of this Data Item Package." | Data Item Type field semantics. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 19 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL | "The K bit in Figure 2 shall be known as the Data Item K-bit. If the defining document for the Data Item Contents specifies that the Simple Object Segmentation Method defined in Annex A is used, then the K bit shall take the meaning specified in Annex A; otherwise its meaning is as specified by the document that defines the contents of the Data Item Package indicated by the Data Item Type value." | K-bit definition. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 20 | ST 2110-41 | 5.4 | SHALL NOT (negation) | "Indicates the total number of 32-bit Data Item Contents elements that follow. This value shall not be equal to zero." | Data Item Length ≥ 1. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 21 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | SHALL | "An SDP object shall be constructed as specified in IETF RFC 4566." | SDP construction per RFC 4566. | Y | SDP composition rule. All RFC 4566 grammar/ordering rules apply. |
| 22 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | SHALL | "The SDP shall comply with the requirements of SMPTE ST 2110-10." | SDP must comply with ST 2110-10. | Y | SDP composition rule. ST 2110-10 SDP requirements (e.g. ts-refclk, mediaclk if any) carry over to -41 SDP. |
| 23 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | MAY | "The SDP may include additional clauses or format-specific media parameters specified in the defining documents for the specific Data Item Types, provided that these additional clauses do not contradict the requirements of this standard." | Per-Data-Item-Type SDP extensions permitted if non-contradictory. | Y | Permissive. Validator should not reject unknown fmtp params on a -41 stream by default — they may be Data Item Type extensions. Contradiction-detection is out of automated scope. |
| 24 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | SHALL | "Senders shall signal the Format Specific Parameter SSN with the value ST2110-41:2024 in the SDP." | Sender SDP must carry `SSN=ST2110-41:2024` as a Format Specific Parameter. | Y | **SDP:** `a=fmtp:<PT>` must contain `SSN=ST2110-41:2024` for senders. Note literal-value conflict with §9.2.2: this clause prescribes `SSN=ST2110-41:2024`, but §9.2.2 (Required Parameters) prescribes `SSN=SMPTE2110-41:2024`. AMBIGUOUS — flag for resolution; §2 says prose is authoritative over tables/figures, so §6 prose form `ST2110-41:2024` arguably wins, but §6's own example also uses `ST2110-41:2024`. |
| 25 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | SHOULD | "Senders should signal the Format Specific Parameter DIT with a value containing a comma-separated list of hexadecimal values of the Data Item Types that might appear in the stream." | DIT is a SHOULD (recommended, not required) for senders. | Y | SHOULD-level — not a validation rejection trigger. If DIT is present, the form rules in row 26 apply. |
| 26 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | SHALL NOT / SHALL (defined-form) | "The hexadecimal values shall not include the leading \"0x\" and any alphabetic characters shall be uppercase. Whitespace characters shall not appear in the comma-separated list of values." | DIT value form: no leading 0x, uppercase hex alpha, no whitespace inside the list. | Y | **SDP:** if `a=fmtp:<PT>` contains `DIT=...`, the value form is constrained — reject `DIT=0x100` (leading 0x), `DIT=100,2000a1` (lowercase hex alpha), `DIT=100, 2000A1` (whitespace inside list). The value is a comma-separated list of hex Data Item Type values. |
| 27 | ST 2110-41 | 6 | (informative example) | "a=fmtp:117 SSN=ST2110-41:2024; DIT=100,2000A1,1013FC,3FFF00" | Worked example: fmtp parameter list separator is "; " between SSN and DIT, list elements separated by comma without spaces. | Y | Informative example. RFC 4566 fmtp syntax governs the param-separator; -41 does not impose a separator on the parameter list as a whole. Internal DIT list separator is comma-without-whitespace (per row 26). |
| 28 | ST 2110-41 | 7 | SHALL | "RTP Streams compliant with this standard shall ensure that their sequence of actual packet transmission instants, as measured on their network egress interface, passes the Network Compatibility Model shown in Figure 3 at all times and in all operating configurations." | Sender egress traffic must pass the Network Compatibility Model. | N | Runtime sender-egress behavior; not SDP signaling. |
| 29 | ST 2110-41 | 7 | SHALL | "Packets from the Sender shall enter a leaky bucket of finite capacity at the instant they are emitted from the Sender." | Bucket-entry semantic. | N | Network model description; not SDP. |
| 30 | ST 2110-41 | 7 | SHALL NOT (negation) | "The value of CINST shall never exceed the CMAX value specified below." | CINST ≤ CMAX always. | N | Network model rule; not SDP. |
| 31 | ST 2110-41 | 7 | SHALL (defined-value) | "For RTP Streams generated in accordance with this standard, the following values shall apply: β = 1.1, TDRAIN = ⌈1 / MAX(800, (RNOMINAL × β))⌉, CMAX = MAX(4, INT(RNOMINAL/43200))" | Fixed bucket-model parameter values. | N | Network model constants; not SDP signaling. |
| 32 | ST 2110-41 | 8.1 | SHALL | "Allocation of entries in this registry is purely administrative and Data Item Type values shall be registered for any request containing all of the required information below. Each Request is for a single Data Item Type registration." | Registry allocation rule. | N | Registry administration; not SDP. |
| 33 | ST 2110-41 | 8.2 | SHALL (defined-range) | "The Data Item Type range 0x000000 through 0x0FFFFF is reserved for allocation by SMPTE for Data Item Types associated with SMPTE technical documents. The Data Item syntax and semantics of such types shall be defined by a SMPTE technical document." | Range 0x000000–0x0FFFFF reserved for SMPTE-defined Data Item Types; their syntax/semantics must be in a SMPTE document. | N | Registry partitioning. The numeric range bounds Data Item Type *values* carried inside RTP packets, but does **not** bound DIT-list values in SDP per se (the SDP DIT list just lists hex values that might appear). Validator could optionally check range-domain but spec does not require SDP to enforce it. |
| 34 | ST 2110-41 | 8.2 | SHALL (required-info) | "The registration information for such a type shall include: the Data Item Type (number) allocated by SMPTE HQ; brief textual description; reference to the defining SMPTE technical document or clause thereof" | Registry record fields for SMPTE-allocated types. | N | Bullet-binding: intro clause "The registration information for such a type shall include:" — these are registry-record contents, not SDP fields. |
| 35 | ST 2110-41 | 8.3 | SHALL (defined-range) | "The Data Item Type range 0x100000 through 0x1FFFFF is reserved for allocation by SMPTE for Data Item Types requested by other user organizations." | Range 0x100000–0x1FFFFF for user-organization types. | N | Registry partitioning; not SDP enforcement. |
| 36 | ST 2110-41 | 8.3 | SHALL (required-info) | "The registration information for such a type shall include: the Data Item Type (number) allocated by SMPTE HQ; brief textual description; reference to the defining technical document or section/clause thereof" | Registry record fields for user-organization types. | N | Bullet-binding: intro clause is "The registration information for such a type shall include:" — registry-record contents, not SDP fields. |
| 37 | ST 2110-41 | 8.4 | SHALL (defined-range) | "The Data Item Type range 0x200000 through 0x2FFFFF is reserved for allocation by SMPTE for Data Item Types requested by individuals and corporations." | Range 0x200000–0x2FFFFF for private (individual/corporate) types. | N | Registry partitioning; not SDP enforcement. |
| 38 | ST 2110-41 | 8.4 | SHALL (required-info) | "The public registration information for such a type shall include: the Data Item Type (number) allocated by SMPTE HQ; brief textual description; A contact name and email address for information purposes; (Optional but highly encouraged) URL or other reference to a defining document" | Registry record fields for private types. | N | Bullet-binding: intro clause "The public registration information for such a type shall include:" — registry-record contents, not SDP fields. |
| 39 | ST 2110-41 | 8.5 | SHALL NOT (reserved) | "The Data Item Type range 0x300000 through 0x3FEFFF is reserved for future use." | Range 0x300000–0x3FEFFF reserved (not used per §2 "reserved" definition). | N | Registry partitioning; per §2 row 1, "reserved" = not used. SDP DIT list inclusion of such values would imply non-conformant Data Item Types in the stream. AMBIGUOUS as an SDP-level check — spec does not say SDP DIT must be only registered types. |
| 40 | ST 2110-41 | 8.6 | (permission) | "The Data Item Type range 0x3FF000 through 0x3FFFFF is for experimental use. These Data Item Types may be used on an experimental basis during the development of new formats and applications without the need to register." | Experimental range 0x3FF000–0x3FFFFF. | N | Permissive; not SDP. |
| 41 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.1 | defined-value | "Type Name: application / Subtype Name: ST2110-41" | IANA media type = `application/ST2110-41`. | Y | **SDP:** encoding-name in `a=rtpmap:<PT> <encoding>/<rate>` for -41 is `ST2110-41`. Media-line should be `m=application <port> RTP/AVP <PT>` (i.e. `m=application`, not `m=video`). AMBIGUOUS: §9.2.1 prescribes the media type registration but does not explicitly bind `m=` to `application` in normative SDP text — that binding follows from RFC 4566 §5.14 (m-line media type maps to IANA media top-level type) by reference through §6 row 21. |
| 42 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.2 | SHALL | "rate: RTP timestamp clock rate, as specified in Clause 5.3 of this document. The rate parameter shall appear in the rtpmap clause of the SDP." | `rate` parameter required in `a=rtpmap`. | Y | **SDP:** `a=rtpmap:<PT> ST2110-41/<rate>` — the `<rate>` token must be present. (Always required by RFC 4566 rtpmap syntax anyway; this restates.) |
| 43 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.2 | required-param (defined-value) | "SSN: The full SMPTE standard number (including year) associated with the stream. SSN=SMPTE2110-41:2024 for streams compliant to this specification." | SSN is required and its value is `SMPTE2110-41:2024` per §9.2.2. | Y | **SDP:** AMBIGUOUS literal-value conflict with §6 row 24: §6 prose and example use `SSN=ST2110-41:2024`; §9.2.2 prose uses `SSN=SMPTE2110-41:2024`. §2 normative-precedence rule states prose is authoritative — but both citations are prose. §6 is the body-of-standard clause normatively requiring SSN; §9.2.2 is the IANA registration template. **Flag for resolution** before enforcing literal SSN value. A defensible validator accepts either `ST2110-41:2024` or `SMPTE2110-41:2024` and warns; a strict validator follows §6's literal as it is the operative requirement clause. |
| 44 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.3 | optional-param | "DIT: The comma-separated list of Data Item Types, as specified in Clause 6 of this document." | DIT is optional. | Y | Confirms §6 DIT-form rules apply when DIT is present. SHOULD-level presence per §6 row 25. |
| 45 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.3 | MUST | "This RTP payload format contains a multiplex of different application data elements. Some data element definition documents may specify additional format-specific media parameters, which if present, must be included in the a=fmtp clause of the SDP." | Per-Data-Item additional fmtp params (when defined by that Data Item's document) must live in `a=fmtp`. | Y | **SDP:** confirms that Data Item-specific fmtp parameters are conveyed via `a=fmtp`, not a separate attribute. Reinforces §6 row 23 permissiveness. |
| 46 | ST 2110-41 | 9.2.11 | (restriction) | "It is restricted to use within the context of RTP framing and is defined only for transfer via RTP as defined in IETF RFC 3550. Transport within other framing protocols is not defined." | Media type only valid over RTP. | Y | Implies `m=application <port> RTP/AVP …` (or RTP-bearing profile) — non-RTP transports for `application/ST2110-41` are not defined. Edge case; rejection criterion only if proto is plainly non-RTP. |
| 47 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "Each successive Data Item Package of the same Data Item Type shall contain one segment of the larger application data object. The contents of the larger object shall be split into 32-bit words, and each segment shall consist of one or more successive 32-bit words." | Simple Object Segmentation packaging rule. | N | RTP payload structure (Annex A normative but content-level); not SDP. |
| 48 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "The size of the segments may be variable from Data Item Package to Data Item Package but each Data Item Package shall be smaller than the maximum size specified in Clause 5.4." | Per-segment size bound. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 49 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "Each Data Item Package shall contain a 32-bit Segment Data Offset and one Segment of the length indicated by the Segment Data Offset." | Segmented package layout. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 50 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "When using the Simple Object Segmentation Method, the Data Item K-bit shall be set to 1 on the last segment of the application object, and set to zero otherwise." | K-bit binding when segmentation is in use. | N | RTP payload byte semantics; not SDP. |
| 51 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "This shall indicate the location of the first 32-bit word of the Segment Contents within the larger application object. The units of the Segment Data Offset shall be 32-bit words." | Segment Data Offset units and semantics. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 52 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "The number of Segment Contents words within each Data Item Package shall be determined by subtracting 2 from the Data Item Length field." | Segment-content length derivation. | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. |
| 53 | ST 2110-41 | A | SHALL | "If the application object length is not evenly divisible by 32 bits, then padding bytes of value 0T shall be added at the end of the application object during the encapsulation process in order to force the total length to be divisible by 32 bits." | Padding rule (32-bit alignment) — value `0T` (verbatim from doc; likely OCR of `0x0` or `0`). | N | RTP payload structure; not SDP. Verbatim quote preserves OCR oddity `0T`. |

## Totals

- **Total clauses**: 53
- **SDP-relevant (SDP? = Y)**: 13 (rows 5, 7, 13, 21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46) — recount: 16 marked Y
- **AMBIGUOUS / flagged**: 3 (rows 24, 41, 43 — primarily the SSN literal-value conflict between §6 and §9.2.2; and the m-line binding implied by §9.2.1 only via RFC 4566 §5.14)

Let me recount precisely the SDP=Y rows by listing: 5, 7, 13, 21, 22, 23, 24, 25, 26, 27, 41, 42, 43, 44, 45, 46 → **16 SDP-Y**.

## Observations

1. **SSN literal-value conflict (HIGH priority for Phase 2)**. §6 says `SSN=ST2110-41:2024`; §9.2.2 (Required Parameters) says `SSN=SMPTE2110-41:2024`. The §6 example is consistent with §6's prose (`ST2110-41:2024`). §2 says prose > tables > figures; both clauses are prose. The operative *requirement* clause is §6 ("Senders shall signal…"); §9.2.2 is the IANA template wording. A pragmatic strict validator may enforce §6's literal value while accepting either form. **Flag for parser-side decision**: which literal to require, whether to warn-only, and how to surface the conflict.
2. **DIT form rules in §6 are tight and testable** — no leading `0x`, uppercase hex alpha, no whitespace. These are SHALL/SHALL-NOT and directly bind DIT values that appear in `a=fmtp`. Good candidates for a defined-form validator (only when DIT is present; DIT itself is SHOULD-level).
3. **DIT is SHOULD-level**, not SHALL — absence of DIT must not cause rejection. SSN is SHALL-level — absence of SSN on a -41 stream is a rejection per §6.
4. **§6 row 23 (MAY include additional clauses)** is a strong anti-overreach signal: per-Data-Item-Type fmtp parameters must be tolerated. The validator should not blanket-reject unknown fmtp keys on a `ST2110-41` rtpmap.
5. **m-line binding for `application/ST2110-41` is implied, not stated.** §9.2.1 fixes the IANA top-level type to `application`. RFC 4566 §5.14 binds the m-line `<media>` token to IANA top-level type. Combination → `m=application`. There is no direct -41 clause forbidding `m=video <port> RTP/AVP <PT>` with rtpmap encoding `ST2110-41`, but it would be inconsistent with the registered media-type top-level. Flag for Phase 2 design decision.
6. **§5.4 UDP size limit references ST 2110-10** — the actual size constant is in -10, not -41. SDP doesn't directly carry MTU; not an SDP-level check.
7. **Data Item Type range partitioning (§8.2–§8.6)** is registry/value-domain, not an SDP constraint per se. The spec does not require SDP DIT list values to be only "registered" values, nor to be confined to in-range values — the DIT list is descriptive ("might appear"), and the spec explicitly allows experimental and reserved-range usage. SDP-level enforcement would be over-strict.
8. **Round-trip serialization concern**: §6's example uses `a=fmtp:117 SSN=ST2110-41:2024; DIT=100,2000A1,1013FC,3FFF00` with a `; ` (semicolon + space) parameter separator. RFC 4566 fmtp value is a free-form `<format specific parameters>` string; spaces around `;` are not mandated. Serializer should preserve and round-trip whatever form the parser accepted.
9. **Cross-spec inheritance via §5.1 + §6 → ST 2110-10**: a -41 SDP must pass ST 2110-10 SDP rules (e.g. PTP/`ts-refclk`, session/media `mediaclk` if -10 mandates them, `source-filter` if applicable). Phase 2 should ensure the -41 validation path runs ST 2110-10 first.
10. **No `m=application` is explicitly written in -41 prose** — the binding is registration-derived. Worth confirming when -41 IPMX TR-10-10 (HDMI InfoFrames) builds on this.

---


# SMPTE — codec references

## SMPTE ST 2042-1:2012 + ST 2110-43:2021 (Codec specs)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_codecs.md`_

# Audit Inventory — Codec Specs (ST 2042-1 VC-2, ST 2110-43 TTML)

Phase 1: enumeration of normative clauses that touch (or could touch) SDP signalling. Comparison to the `parse_sdp` parser is Phase 2 and is performed in the main thread.

Sources consulted (primary):

- SMPTE ST 2042-1:2012 — markdown at `/Users/andrewstarks/Library/CloudStorage/Dropbox/Personal/Claude/Macnica/Standards Related/smpte_standards_internal/st-2042-1-2012.md`
- SMPTE ST 2110-43:2021 — PDF at `/Users/andrewstarks/Library/CloudStorage/Dropbox/Personal/Claude/Macnica/Standards Related/smpte_standards_internal/st2110-43-2021.pdf` (extracted with `pdftotext -layout`; markdown not yet available).

Both specs were re-checked for markdown availability at start of walk: ST 2042-1 has `.md`; ST 2110-43 does not.

## Conformance vocabulary preamble (informational)

Both specs declare standard SMPTE conformance vocabulary in their "Conformance Notation" / Foreword: "shall" / "shall not" = strict requirement; "should" / "should not" = recommendation; "may" / "need not" = permission; "reserved" = not currently defined, shall not be used; "forbidden" = reserved AND will never be defined. ST 2042-1 §2 and ST 2110-43 Foreword. (See rows 1 and 24 below.)

## Table

| # | Spec | § | Verb | Verbatim quote | Summary | SDP? | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 2 (Conformance Notation) | SHALL (definition) | "The keywords \"shall\" and \"shall not\" indicate requirements strictly to be followed in order to conform to the document and from which no deviation is permitted" | Conformance vocabulary definition. | N | Meta — defines verb semantics for the rest of the document. |
| 2 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 2 | SHALL (reserved/forbidden) | "The keyword \"reserved\" indicates a provision that is not defined at this time, shall not be used, and may be defined in the future. The keyword \"forbidden\" indicates \"reserved\" and in addition indicates that the provision will never be defined in the future." | Defines "reserved" / "forbidden" semantics. | N | Meta. Out of SDP scope. |
| 3 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 1 (Scope) | descriptive | "This standard defines the VC-2 video compression system through the stream syntax, entropy coding, coefficient unpacking process and picture decoding process." | Scope statement: bitstream-level codec definition. | N | Confirms that the bulk of ST 2042-1 is bitstream/decoder behavior, not SDP. Only the value sets that downstream payload-format documents (e.g. RFC 8450) cite are SDP-relevant. |
| 4 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 1 | descriptive | "Additional standards and recommended practices may define specific constraints on the encoding for particular applications." | Acknowledges that companion documents (ST 2042-2 levels, RTP payload formats) layer on top. | N | Context — explains why concrete level numbers and the SDP wire-form live elsewhere. |
| 5 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 6 (Overall) | SHALL | "the term \"core syntax\" shall refer to the Main and Simple profiles, while the term \"low delay syntax\" shall refer to the Low Delay and High Quality profiles." | Defines mapping of syntax-category terms to the four profile names. | N | Pure terminology. The names themselves (Main, Simple, Low Delay, High Quality) are what matter; the syntax-category grouping is internal to ST 2042-1. |
| 6 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1 (Parse Parameters) | SHALL | "This section specifies the structure of the parse parameters, which shall be defined as follows: [parse_parameters() table: major_version, minor_version, profile, level — all UInt via read_uint()]" | Establishes that profile and level are unsigned-integer fields in the bitstream parse parameters. | N | The integer encoding is in the bitstream; SDP `a=fmtp` uses textual names per the RTP payload format (RFC 8450). |
| 7 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1 | SHALL | "The parse parameters data values shall be constant (byte-for-byte identical) for all instances of the sequence header within a VC-2 sequence." | Per-sequence parse-parameter stability. | N | Bitstream-internal consistency, not SDP. |
| 8 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1 | SHOULD | "For VC-2 Stream interchange, the VC-2 Profile and Level values should also be identical for all VC-2 sequences within a VC-2 stream." | Recommendation that profile/level be stable across sequences in a stream. | N | "Should", not "shall"; also a stream-level not SDP-level constraint. |
| 9 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 (Version Number) | SHALL | "The version number of the VC-2 syntax specification shall be used by the decoder to determine whether it can decode the sequence." | Decoder requirement on use of version number. | N | Decoder behavior, not SDP. |
| 10 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL | "The major version number shall define the version of the syntax with which the stream complies." | Defines purpose of major_version field. | N | Bitstream field semantics. |
| 11 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL | "All minor versions of the specification shall be functionally compatible with earlier minor versions with the same major version number." | Minor version forward-compatibility constraint. | N | Spec-versioning rule. |
| 12 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL NOT | "Later minor version numbers shall not contain new features or new normative provisions." | Prohibition on substantive change between minor versions. | N | Editorial rule. |
| 13 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL | "Functional compatibility shall imply that a decoder with the same major version number and later minor version number as a stream shall be capable of decoding the stream and producing decoded pictures that are substantially equivalent to that of a decoder with the same version number as the stream." | Functional compatibility decoder requirement. | N | Decoder semantics. |
| 14 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL | "If the stream includes High Quality Pictures, that is the Parse Info Header (section 10.4) includes the parse code (0xE8) for High Quality Pictures (table 10.1), then the major version number of a stream compliant with this version of the VC-2 standard shall be 2. Otherwise, if the stream includes no High Quality Pictures, the major version number of a stream shall be 1." | Defined value set: major_version ∈ {1, 2} keyed on presence of High Quality Pictures. | AMBIGUOUS | If a payload-format spec exposes a `version` (or similar) fmtp parameter, this would constrain its legal value set. RFC 8450 fmtp does not currently expose `version` — but worth flagging. Marked AMBIGUOUS rather than Y. |
| 15 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.1 | SHALL | "The minor version number of a stream compliant with this version of the VC-2 standard shall be 0." | Defined value: minor_version = 0 for this edition. | AMBIGUOUS | Same caveat as row 14 — bitstream value, not currently in any fmtp parameter. |
| 16 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.2 (Profiles and Levels) | SHALL | "The profile shall define the toolset that is sufficient to decode a VC-2 sequence." | Profile semantics. | N | Definitional. |
| 17 | ST 2042-1:2012 | 11.1.2 | SHALL | "The level shall define decoder resources (picture and data buffers; computational resources) sufficient to decode a sequence." | Level semantics. | N | Definitional. |
| 18 | ST 2042-1:2012 | Annex D (intro) | SHALL | "A VC-2 decoder shall support one or more different profiles and levels. Profiles and levels determine which tools, syntax elements and structures shall be supported, and what decoder resources (computational and memory) are required." | Decoder must support at least one profile and level. | N | Decoder capability statement. |
| 19 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1 (Profiles) | SHALL (defined value set) | "VC-2 defines four profiles, main, simple, low delay and high quality, corresponding to different picture types. These shall satisfy the following conditions: – A low delay profile VC-2 sequence shall set state[profile] equal to a value of 0 in the parse parameters (Section 10.4) for each sequence header in the sequence. – A simple profile sequence shall set state[profile] equal to a value of 1 in the parse parameters for each sequence header in the sequence. – A main profile sequence shall set state[profile] equal to a value of 2 in the parse parameters for each sequence header in the sequence. – A high quality profile sequence shall set state[profile] equal to a value of 3 in the parse parameters for each sequence header in the sequence." | Defines the four canonical profile names ("main", "simple", "low delay", "high quality") and their bitstream integer codes (2, 1, 0, 3). | Y | **Authoritative name list.** Whatever RTP payload format / fmtp grammar names VC-2 profiles in SDP, it must draw from this set. The integers (0/1/2/3) are bitstream, but the names propagate. Bullet-binding check: the bulleted list attaches to "These shall satisfy the following conditions" — that clause is the intro for the four bullets. Verified. |
| 20 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1 | SHALL | "A VC-2 sequence shall comply with one of the supported profiles." | Sequence must conform to exactly one profile. | N | Bitstream constraint; an SDP-level cross-check would be circular unless an fmtp parameter were present. |
| 21 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1.1 (Low Delay Profile) | SHALL | "A low delay profile sequence shall contain only those data units whose parse codes are listed in Table D.1." and "A low delay profile sequence shall contain only low delay pictures." | Low-delay profile data-unit and picture-type constraint. | N | Bitstream content rule. |
| 22 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1.2 (Simple Profile) | SHALL | "A simple profile sequence shall contain only those data units whose parse codes are listed in Table D.2." and "A simple profile sequence shall contain core syntax pictures that do not use arithmetic coding." | Simple profile data-unit and entropy-coding constraint. | N | Bitstream content rule. |
| 23 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1.3 (Main Profile) | SHALL / MAY | "A main profile sequence may contain any of the data units whose parse codes are listed in Table D.3." and "A main profile sequence shall contain core syntax pictures that use arithmetic coding." | Main profile data-unit and entropy-coding constraint. | N | Bitstream content rule. |
| 24 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.1.4 (High Quality Profile) | SHALL | "A high Quality profile sequence shall contain only those data units whose parse codes are listed in Table D.4." and "A high quality profile sequence shall contain only high quality pictures." | High Quality profile data-unit and picture-type constraint. | N | Bitstream content rule. |
| 25 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.2 (Levels) | SHALL | "A given value of level shall define constraints on the decoder resources required to decode a compliant sequence. The parameter values (or range of values) that are constrained for each level shall be defined in associated SMPTE documents." | ST 2042-1 itself does **not** enumerate level numeric values or names; level definitions are delegated to companion documents (ST 2042-2, etc.). | N | Critical for scoping: any fmtp `level` value-set constraint is **not** in ST 2042-1; it is in ST 2042-2 or whichever profile-specific level doc applies. Out of scope for this row in the audit (a different agent walks ST 2042-2 if needed). Note: ST 2042-1:2012 does **not** mention "sublevel" anywhere; sublevels are defined elsewhere. |
| 26 | ST 2042-1:2012 | D.2 (Note) | informative | "Note: Generalized level values are defined in the companion standard SMPTE ST 2042-2. Specialized level values are defined in other associated SMPTE documents." | Cross-reference. | N | Note paragraph — explicitly informative per §2. |
| 27 | ST 2042-1:2012 | various (e.g. §11.1, §11.3) | SHALL | (Numerous bitstream syntax SHALLs: Sequence Header structure, source_parameters layout, parse_info header structure, transform parameters, wavelet coefficient unpacking, IDWT, picture decoding, arithmetic coding state machine, exp-Golomb code definitions, predefined video formats in Annex C, default quantization matrices in Annex E) | Collectively: how a VC-2 bitstream is parsed and decoded. | N | Out-of-SDP-scope per audit rule: "most of a CODEC spec is bitstream / encoding behavior, NOT SDP signalling." None of these constrain a value that appears in any current SDP `a=fmtp` parameter for VC-2 (per RFC 8450). Recorded as a single row to avoid flooding the inventory; the bitstream/encoding clauses are not individually audit-relevant. |
| 28 | ST 2110-43:2021 | Foreword | SHALL (definition) | "The keywords \"shall\" and \"shall not\" indicate requirements strictly to be followed in order to conform to the document and from which no deviation is permitted." | Conformance vocabulary. | N | Meta. |
| 29 | ST 2110-43:2021 | Foreword | SHALL | "Unless otherwise specified, the order of precedence of the types of normative information in this document shall be as follows: Normative prose shall be the authoritative definition; Tables shall be next; then formal languages; then figures; and then any other language forms." | Normative-source precedence (prose > tables > formal language > figures). | N | Meta. |
| 30 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 1 (Scope) | descriptive | "This standard specifies the real-time, RTP-based transport of Timed Text Markup Language for captions and subtitles in systems conforming to SMPTE ST 2110-10." | Scope: TTML captions/subtitles over RTP within ST 2110. | N | Scope statement, not a SHALL on SDP form. |
| 31 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.1 (General) | SHALL | "Timed Text shall be expressed in Timed Text Markup Language 2 (TTML2) as defined in W3C TTML2." | The carried payload must be TTML2 (not TTML1, not other markup). | Y | This is a stream-content rule, but it has SDP consequences: the SDP encoding-name and RFC 8759 payload semantics presuppose TTML2. From an SDP-grammar perspective, this constrains the choice of payload format (RFC 8759) that an SDP `a=rtpmap` may select to carry a 2110-43-conformant stream. |
| 32 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.1 | SHALL | "The Timed Text Markup Language shall be transported using RTP with the payload format and SDP defined in IETF RFC 8759." | **Authoritative pointer** to RFC 8759 for both the RTP payload format AND the SDP form. | Y | The entire SDP signalling for ST 2110-43 is delegated to RFC 8759. The SDP-relevant clauses ultimately live in RFC 8759 (a separate walk); this clause's role for SDP is "use RFC 8759's signalling — no substitute is permitted." A 2110-43 SDP must use RFC 8759's `m=` line / `a=rtpmap` encoding name / `a=fmtp` parameter form. |
| 33 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.1 | SHALL | "The RTP stream and its SDP shall be in conformance with SMPTE ST 2110-10." | Forces ST 2110-10 SDP conformance (PTP `a=ts-refclk:ptp=...`, `a=mediaclk:direct=0`, etc.) on top of RFC 8759. | Y | Cross-tier rule: a 2110-43 SDP must validate as 2110-10 as well. This is how 2110-43 plugs into the rest of the ST 2110 family in SDP. |
| 34 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.2 (Additional constraints) | SHALL | "The Timed Text Markup Language shall conform to one of the Profiles of TTML2 defined in W3C IMSC1.2." | TTML2 content must be one of the IMSC1.2 profiles. | N | Content (XML profile) rule, enforced by inspecting the TTML payload, not the SDP. RFC 8759's fmtp does not currently expose an IMSC profile parameter that would let SDP validate this. |
| 35 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.2 | SHALL | "The RTP Clock used to generate the RTP timestamp shall have a frequency of 90 kHz." | **Fixed RTP clock rate: 90 000 Hz.** | Y | Directly constrains `a=rtpmap:<pt> <encoding-name>/<clock-rate>` — the clock-rate field must be 90000 for any 2110-43 stream. This is the strongest SDP-visible constraint in the document. |
| 36 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 4.3 (Keep alive mechanism) | MAY | "Packets with Length field set to zero and Marker bit set to 1 may be sent between TTML2 documents if required." | Optional RTP-packet-level keepalive mechanism. | N | RTP-packet field, not SDP. Permissive, no value-set or SDP form to validate. |
| 37 | ST 2110-43:2021 | 5 (Informative) | — | (entirety of §5 — TTML2 document timing, synchronization with related media streams) | Informative discussion of how RTP timestamp lines up with TTML document timing and with Reference Clock-synchronized peers. | N | Section is explicitly labeled "(Informative)". Not normative, by §Foreword rule. |

## Subtotals

### ST 2042-1:2012 (VC-2)

- Rows: 27 (rows 1–27).
- SDP? = Y count: **1** (row 19 — the canonical profile-name set).
- AMBIGUOUS count: **2** (rows 14 and 15 — major/minor version defined values; could become Y if a future fmtp parameter exposes them).
- Decisive observation: of a ~137-page bitstream/decoder spec, only the four profile-name strings ("main", "simple", "low delay", "high quality") cross into SDP via the RFC 8450 fmtp grammar. Levels (and sublevels) are explicitly delegated to companion documents (D.2 and the §D.2 Note). ST 2042-1:2012 does **not** define "sublevel" at all — that term is introduced in ST 2042-2 / VSF TR-08 territory.

### ST 2110-43:2021 (TTML over ST 2110)

- Rows: 10 (rows 28–37).
- SDP? = Y count: **4** (rows 31, 32, 33, 35).
- AMBIGUOUS count: **0**.
- Decisive observation: ST 2110-43 is a thin (5-page) wrapper that delegates almost the entire SDP wire-form to RFC 8759. Its standalone SDP-validatable constraints reduce to:
  1. Encoding name selected via `a=rtpmap` must be RFC 8759's TTML payload format (row 32).
  2. Clock rate on the `a=rtpmap` must be exactly 90000 (row 35).
  3. The SDP must additionally conform to ST 2110-10 (row 33), which a 2110-10 walker has separately enumerated.
  Row 31 (TTML2-not-TTML1) is implicitly handled by row 32: RFC 8759 is TTML2-specific by construction.

### Combined totals

- Total rows: **37**.
- SDP? = Y: **5** (1 from ST 2042-1; 4 from ST 2110-43).
- AMBIGUOUS: **2** (both from ST 2042-1, both version-number related).

## Observations for Phase 2 (main thread comparison)

1. **VC-2 SDP signalling is downstream of ST 2042-1, not in it.** The actual fmtp parameter grammar for VC-2 lives in IETF RFC 8450 ("RTP Payload Format for VC-2 HQ Profile"). Phase 2 should:
   - Confirm that `parse_sdp` either does not validate VC-2 fmtp at all (which is consistent with the strictness principle and the spec audits already shipped — VC-2 is outside the current scope of 2110-22 in `parse_sdp`), OR
   - If it does, verify that its profile-name value set matches exactly the four strings normalized from D.1: `main`, `simple`, `low delay`, `high quality` (verbatim names from §D.1 prose; the wire-form casing/spelling for fmtp is set by RFC 8450 and may differ slightly — e.g. `LowDelay` vs `low_delay`). **Do not invent a name list from ST 2042-1; the RFC 8450 grammar is authoritative for fmtp tokens.**
   - Confirm that any level-value validation cites ST 2042-2 (or the applicable specialized level doc), **not** ST 2042-1. ST 2042-1 §D.2 is explicit that 2042-1 does not enumerate level values.
   - "Sublevel" must not cite ST 2042-1; it is not defined there.

2. **ST 2110-43 fmtp signalling is fully delegated to RFC 8759.** Phase 2 should confirm that any TTML-related SDP handling in `parse_sdp`:
   - Treats RFC 8759 as the authoritative payload-format grammar (not ST 2110-43).
   - If ST 2110-43 validation is implemented as a tier, requires `clock-rate == 90000` on `a=rtpmap` (row 35) — this is the one ST 2110-43-specific SDP-grammar check that does not also follow from RFC 8759 or ST 2110-10.
   - Ensures cross-tier validation: a 2110-43-marked stream must also pass ST 2110-10 (row 33).

3. **Bullet-binding check (audit rule 3).** Only one bulleted normative list exists in the SDP-relevant material: §D.1's four bullets on the profile/value mapping. Intro clause is "VC-2 defines four profiles, main, simple, low delay and high quality, corresponding to different picture types. These shall satisfy the following conditions:" — the bullets attach to "These shall satisfy the following conditions," and substitute cleanly. No false-bullet-binding trap detected.

4. **No false findings from "the spec is silent."** ST 2042-1 §D.2 is **explicit** that 2042-1 is silent on level numeric values (it delegates to companion documents) — that's not "silent" in the bug-trap sense; it's an explicit delegation. Any audit finding that wants to say "ST 2042-1 doesn't say X about a level value" is correct but uninteresting: 2042-1 was never going to say it. The right cite is ST 2042-2 (or the applicable level doc).

5. **Out-of-SDP-scope flagging for ST 2042-1.** Row 27 collapses the entire bitstream/decoder/encoder body of ST 2042-1 (parse-info headers, sequence-header layout, source-parameters table, wavelet transform, IDWT, arithmetic decoder, exp-Golomb codes, predefined video formats in Annex C, default quantization matrices in Annex E, etc.) into a single audit row. This is intentional: enumerating each SHALL individually would produce 50+ rows that all answer "N" with the same reason ("bitstream/decoder behavior, not SDP"), with zero audit value. If Phase 2 later finds that `parse_sdp` cites a specific ST 2042-1 §X.Y for an SDP-level check, that specific clause can be looked up in the markdown on demand.

## Output

This file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_codecs.md`.

# SMPTE — supporting

## SMPTE ST 2022-7:2013 (Seamless Protection)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_st2022-7.md`_

# Audit Inventory: SMPTE ST 2022-7:2013

**Spec**: SMPTE ST 2022-7:2013 — Seamless Protection Switching of SMPTE ST 2022 IP Datagrams
**Source**: `/Users/andrewstarks/Library/CloudStorage/Dropbox/Personal/Claude/Macnica/Standards Related/smpte_standards_internal/smpte2022-7-2013.pdf` (converted via `pdftotext -layout` to `/tmp/st2022-7-2013.txt`)
**Approved**: October 11, 2013
**Pages**: 13

## Inventory of normative clauses

| # | Spec | § | Verb | Verbatim quote | Summary | SDP? | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §2 (Conformance Notation) | shall not / "no deviation" | "The keywords \"shall\" and \"shall not\" indicate requirements strictly to be followed in order to conform to the document and from which no deviation is permitted." | Defines the meaning of `shall`/`shall not` for the document; meta-clause, not a substantive requirement. | N | Meta — conformance language definition, not an SDP constraint. |
| 2 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §2 (Conformance Notation) | shall not (reserved) | "The keyword \"reserved\" indicates a provision that is not defined at this time, shall not be used, and may be defined in the future." | Defines the meaning of `reserved`; meta-clause. | N | Meta — no reserved provisions are themselves enumerated in the document body. |
| 3 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §2 (Conformance Notation) | shall (order of precedence) | "Unless otherwise specified, the order of precedence of the types of normative information in this document shall be as follows: Normative prose shall be the authoritative definition; Tables shall be next; followed by formal languages; then figures; and then any other language forms." | Defines how to resolve conflicts between prose, tables, formal language, figures. | N | Meta — interpretation rule, not an SDP constraint. |
| 4 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (transmit at least two streams) | "The transmitter shall transmit at least two streams, each containing copies of each SMPTE 2022 RTP datagram." | Transmitter MUST emit at least two redundant streams, each carrying copies of every RTP datagram of the source. | Y | This is the foundational basis for `a=group:DUP` in SDP: an SDP advertising ST 2022-7 redundancy must enumerate two (or more) media descriptions and group them. The clause itself does not name `a=group:DUP`; binding to SDP is by way of RFC 7104. AMBIGUOUS as to whether more than two is permitted ("at least two") — the document discusses only the two-stream case throughout. |
| 5 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (identical RTP header + payload) | "The RTP header and the RTP payload shall be identical for each datagram copy." | All redundant RTP datagrams MUST have byte-identical RTP headers and byte-identical RTP payloads across all copies. | Y | The single most important SDP consequence: the two streams of an `a=group:DUP` MUST be coherent at the RTP layer. This forces equality of payload type number, payload format (`a=rtpmap`), payload format parameters (`a=fmtp`), RTP clock rate (`a=rtpmap` rate field), and any payload-format-specific signalling. The clause is at the RTP-datagram level; the SDP must describe streams that *can* produce byte-identical datagrams. AMBIGUOUS as written: the spec does not enumerate which SDP attributes must therefore match — it asserts byte-equality of the on-wire RTP. Cross-stream SDP-attribute coherence is an inference, not a literal SDP clause. |
| 6 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | (no constraint) Ethernet/IP headers | "The seamless reconstruction method described herein makes no assumptions about the Ethernet or IP headers of the source streams." | The two streams MAY differ in Ethernet/IP headers (different destination IP, different port, different VLAN, etc.). | Y (negative) | This is the *only* spec-text basis for permitting differing `c=` (connection address) and `m=` port across the two grouped media — i.e. the two halves of an `a=group:DUP` SDP are not required to share IP/port. Restated more strongly in Annex B (informative). |
| 7 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (HBR RTP timestamp required) | "For Class HBR streams, as specified in SMPTE ST 2022-6 the RTP timestamp shall be required." | For Class HBR (per §5.1: ST 2022-5 or ST 2022-6 streams ≥ 270 Mbps), the RTP timestamp field MUST be populated (delegates to ST 2022-6). | N | RTP wire-level requirement, not an SDP field. ST 2022-6 governs the wire format. No SDP attribute carries this. |
| 8 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (HBR VSID identical) | "Furthermore, the VSID field as defined in SMPTE ST 2022-6 is part of the RTP payload, and shall be identical across the datagram copies." | The Video Source ID (VSID) carried inside the ST 2022-6 RTP payload MUST be byte-identical across all redundant copies. | N | This is a re-statement of clause #5 specialized to a payload-format-defined sub-field. It lives in the RTP payload, not in SDP. Listed as a separate normative clause because the spec calls it out explicitly ("Furthermore… shall be identical"). |
| 9 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §6 (Creation of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (SBR — delegated) | "For Class SBR streams, the RTP timestamp requirement is as stated in the relevant SMPTE 2022 standard." | For Class SBR (ST 2022-1/-2/-3/-4 streams < 270 Mbps) the RTP timestamp obligation is whatever the underlying spec says — ST 2022-7 itself imposes no additional timestamp obligation on SBR. | N | RTP-layer delegation; no SDP attribute. |
| 10 | ST 2022-7:2013 | §7 (Reception of Streams for Seamless Reconstruction) | shall (compliant receiver PD support) | "A compliant receiver for Classes A, B, or C shall support Seamless Reconstruction from streams that maintain a PD value of less than or equal to those specified in the table below for its classification." | A receiver claiming Class A / B / C MUST be able to perform seamless reconstruction when the path differential (PD = \|P1 − P2\|) is within its class limit (Table: Class A ≤ 10 ms SBR/HBR; Class B ≤ 50 ms SBR/HBR; Class C ≤ 450 ms SBR / ≤ 150 ms HBR). | N | Receiver requirement, not a sender SDP requirement. SDP for ST 2022-7 does not carry a "PD class" advertisement; SMPTE 2110-10 follows the same pattern. No SDP attribute is required by this clause. |

---

## Counts

- **Total normative clauses enumerated**: 10
- **SDP-relevant (Y)**: 3 (rows 4, 5, 6) — plus row 6 is a *permissive* clause (no constraint on IP/port), not a positive obligation.
- **AMBIGUOUS**: 2 (rows 4 and 5)

## Observations

1. **The spec never mentions SDP, `a=group`, `a=rtpmap`, `a=fmtp`, or any SDP attribute.** ST 2022-7 defines wire-level redundancy at the RTP datagram layer. The SDP binding for ST 2022-7 is provided by **IETF RFC 7104** (Duplication Grouping Semantics in SDP), which is *not* normatively referenced by ST 2022-7:2013 (RFC 7104 post-dates ST 2022-7 in any event). Any validator clause that says "ST 2022-7 requires `a=group:DUP`" is mis-cited — ST 2022-7 requires "the transmitter shall transmit at least two streams" (clause #4) and the SDP convention to express that is RFC 7104.

2. **The most-cited ST 2022-7 obligation for SDP is §6 clause #5 ("RTP header and RTP payload shall be identical").** This is wire-level, not SDP-level, but it transitively implies a strong family of SDP coherence properties for the two grouped media: payload type numbers must produce identical RTP headers (so the `a=rtpmap` payload-type number and format must match), payload-format parameters that affect bytes-on-the-wire must match (so `a=fmtp` must match for the parameters that change wire format), and the RTP clock rate must match (so the `a=rtpmap` rate must match). Every one of those is an *inference* from clause #5, not a literal SDP requirement in ST 2022-7. The spec's own answer to "what must the SDP look like?" is silent.

3. **Explicit permission for differing IP/port** (clauses #6 and Annex B): the redundant streams MAY differ in Ethernet/IP headers. So an SDP validator MUST NOT require that the two `m=` lines in an `a=group:DUP` use the same `c=` connection address or the same port. This is the strongest positive SDP-related statement in the entire document, and it is a permission, not a requirement.

4. **The PD class table (§7) is a receiver capability, not an SDP attribute.** ST 2022-7 defines no SDP signalling for path differential or receiver class. SMPTE ST 2110-10 §6 later adopts the "PD < 50 ms" Class B target (or similar) by reference but does not surface it in SDP either.

5. **"At least two streams"** (clause #4) — the document discusses only the two-stream case in all worked examples and Annex A/B narratives, but the normative phrasing is "at least two." A strict reading permits N ≥ 3 streams in an `a=group:DUP`. RFC 7104 likewise permits more than two. The validator should not cap at 2.

6. **No SDP timing signalling is required.** Clauses #7, #8, #9 govern RTP timestamps and payload-internal fields; none of them surface in SDP.

7. **Annexes A through F are explicitly labeled Informative** (per §2: "any section explicitly labeled as 'Informative'"). They contain useful explanatory text (RTP sequence-number rollover, startup PT/EA strategies, network use cases) but **no normative clauses**. None of their material — including the worked Class C startup strategy in Annex A — produces a validator obligation.

8. **Out-of-SDP-scope clauses identified**: clauses #1, #2, #3 (meta — conformance language); #7, #8, #9 (RTP-layer payload fields, not SDP); #10 (receiver capability, not SDP).

9. **Net SDP obligations from ST 2022-7 alone**:
   - (Strong, inferred) Redundant streams in an `a=group:DUP` must be configured such that the two RTP wire streams can be byte-identical — implies coherent payload type, rtpmap, fmtp, and clock.
   - (Permissive) The two streams MAY differ in connection address / port (do not require equality).
   - (Inferential count) ≥ 2 streams, not exactly 2.
   - (Zero) ST 2022-7 itself does not require *any specific SDP attribute*. The `a=group:DUP` convention lives in RFC 7104.

10. **Implication for `parse_sdp` audit**: any ST 2022-7 validator check in the parser that does anything beyond "the streams of an `a=group:DUP` have matching `a=rtpmap` payload type, format, and rate, and matching `a=fmtp`" (inferred from clause #5) needs to cite either RFC 7104 or the relevant downstream spec (ST 2110-10), not ST 2022-7 §6 directly. Citing ST 2022-7 for an SDP attribute requirement is almost always a mis-cite because the spec contains no SDP attribute requirements at all.

---

## SMPTE RP 2110-23/24/25 (Recommended Practices)

_Inventory file: `/tmp/audit_inventory_rp2110.md`_

# Audit Inventory — SMPTE RP 2110-23, RP 2110-24:2023, RP 2110-25:2023

**Source priority**: RP 2110-23 PDF (no markdown on disk) → `pdftotext -layout`. RP 2110-24 and RP 2110-25 markdowns on disk.

It also provides guidance on values for certain Media Type Parameters." — partly SDP-relevant (constrains values of the `width`, `height`, `PAR` media type parameters which appear in `a=fmtp`) |
