| Spec | Count | IDs and reason |
|---|---|---|
| IPMX-JPEG-XS v1.0 | 4 | JX-11 (sublevel-signaling: names MIB but ambiguous re: SDP coupling); JX-15 (TR-8 vs TR-08 numbering); JX-25 (MIB type 0x0003 in §6.1.4 vs 0x0008 in §6.2.3 — likely document inconsistency); JX-26 (forward reference to unpublished TR-10-15); JX-27 (forward reference to TR-10-15) |
| **Total AMBIGUOUS** | **5** | (JX-11, JX-15, JX-25, JX-26, JX-27) |

### [AES67-2013 wording] flags (IPMX-PCM-Audio only)

| Spec | Count | IDs and reason |
|---|---|---|
| IPMX-PCM-Audio v1.0 | 3 | PCM-01 (§3 normative refs do NOT cite AES67 directly — but AES67-2018 is current and the profile's relationship to AES67 is asserted in §9); PCM-46 (§9.1.3 cites "AES67" without version); PCM-47 (§9.2 cites "AES67" without version). The profile defers AES67 conformance to TR-10-3 (which itself should be aligned to AES67-2018) but never names a specific AES67 edition. Flag: in primary AES67-touching clauses, IPMX-PCM-Audio v1.0 references "AES67" un-versioned — if the parser's AES67 fixtures are AES67-2013-era, no harm done at this tier (profile is silent), but the parser may want to verify TR-10-3 itself is AES67-2018-aligned. |

### Bullet-binding `scope:` notes (clauses where bullet-binding affects scope reading)

| # | Clause | Why bullet-binding matters |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | **JX-14 / §6.1.4** | **CANONICAL TRAP. Bullets `transmode / packetmode / profile / level / sublevel / fbblevel` bind to item 1's "shall populate the JPEG-XS Media Info Block (type 0x0003)… including:" — they are RTCP Media Info Block fields, NOT SDP fmtp parameters, despite the section title "Required Sender Signaling (Media Info Block & SDP)". DO NOT generate an SDP-side check for `fbblevel`, `transmode`, `packetmode`, etc., from this clause.** |
| 2 | JX-16 / §6.1.4 | Bullets of the consistency list ("resolution, frame rate, color sampling, bit depth, profile, level, sublevel") bind to "ensuring that: SDP, the Media Info Block, and the actual JPEG-XS stream are consistent in…" — these are *dimensions of consistency*, not new SDP-attribute names. |
| 3 | JX-27 / §6.2.3 | Bullets ("Resolution; Frame rate (grain rate); Color sampling; Component depth; JPEG-XS profile, level, and sublevel") bind to "validated against:" — dimensions to validate, not new SDP attributes. |
| 4 | UV-12 / §6.1.4 | Bullets ("Info Block contents; SDP; Actual stream behavior") bind to "ensuring consistency between:" — categories of artifact, not attribute names. |
| 5 | UV-16 / §6.2.2 | Bullets ("Sampling structure; Bit depth; Colorimetry and transfer characteristics; Active image dimensions") bind to "shall correctly interpret all TR-10-2 format parameters, including:" — TR-10-2 fields the receiver must interpret, not new SDP attributes. |
| 6 | PCM-13 / §6.1.4 | Bullets ("Sample rate; Sample size; Channel count; Packet time; Measured sample rate; Channel order") bind to "shall populate all required PCM Audio Media Info Block fields as defined in TR-10-3, including:" — MIB fields, NOT SDP attributes. Same trap shape as JX-14. |
| 7 | PCM-20 / §6.2.2 | Bullets ("Channel count; Channel order; Sample size; Packet time; Media clock vs RTP clock behavior") bind to "shall correctly interpret all conveyed TR-10-3 parameters, including:" — interpretation list. |
| 8 | PCM-29 / §7.1.2 | Bullets ("Sample rate; Channel count; Bit depth; Packet time") bind to "Transport parameters exposed through NMOS shall match … including:" — NMOS-side dimensions, not new SDP attributes. |

**Total bullet-binding scope: notes: 8** (JX-14 is the canonical trap explicitly called out in the audit prompt and CLAUDE.md).

---

## Observations for the Phase-2 main-thread comparison

1. **No IPMX profile v1.0 clause defines a new SDP attribute or fmtp parameter.** All SDP-form rules at the IPMX tier are delegated to the relevant TR-10 document:
   - IPMX-Uncompressed v1.0 → TR-10-2 (which delegates to ST 2110-20 / RFC 4175)
   - IPMX-JPEG-XS v1.0 → TR-10-11 (and forthcoming TR-10-15) + VSF TR-08 §8.1 + ISO/IEC 21122 (which delegates to ST 2110-22 / BCP-006-01 / RFC 9134)
   - IPMX-PCM-Audio v1.0 → TR-10-3 (which delegates to ST 2110-30 / AES67 / RFC 3551)

2. **The IPMX-tier SDP validation in parse_sdp should therefore be very thin.** Any IPMX-specific SDP check needs to point at a TR-10 clause that owns it. If a check cannot be traced to a TR-10 clause, it is either misplaced at the IPMX tier (should be ST 2110 or RFC 4566 tier) or it is a phantom (the fbblevel case).

3. **The JPEG-XS fbblevel SDP check that was removed (audit finding D2) is correctly removed.** The §6.1.4 bullet list is unambiguously a Media Info Block field enumeration. Verified by:
   - The introducing clause ("shall populate the JPEG-XS Media Info Block (type 0x0003) as defined in TR-10-11 Section 12, including:") substitution test: "shall populate the JPEG-XS Media Info Block, including: fbblevel" parses cleanly as a MIB-population statement.
   - The MIB type number (0x0003) is a TR-10-11 MIB type code, not an SDP construct.
   - §6.1.4's *separate* sentence on SDP ("shall populate the associated SDP fields required by TR-10-11") delegates the SDP set to TR-10-11 — it does NOT extend the bullet list to SDP.

4. **Device-capability vs single-SDP scope.** Many §6.1.1 / §6.2.1 / §6.2.2 clauses say things like "the sender shall support at least one of {Format A, Format B}" or "the receiver shall support both…". These are device-capability assertions visible in NMOS Sender/Receiver Capabilities (BCP-004-01/02) — they cannot be validated from a single SDP because a single SDP describes one stream, not the device's full capability matrix. The parser should NOT attempt to enforce these from SDP.

5. **Resolution/frame-rate "Undefined / Any" reaffirmations (UV-07, UV-17, JX-08, JX-20) are NEGATIVE constraints.** They forbid the parser from imposing a resolution/rate whitelist at the IPMX tier. If parse_sdp currently restricts resolutions or frame rates for IPMX-Uncompressed or IPMX-JPEG-XS, that would be over-strict and should fail audit.

6. **MIB type 0x0003 vs 0x0008 inconsistency (JX-25)** is internal to the JPEG-XS profile doc and does not affect SDP, but it is worth flagging upstream to VSF/AIMS. Per the Appendix A revision note ("Fixed incorrect CBR Media Infoblock type"), §6.1.4's 0x0003 is the corrected value; §6.2.3's 0x0008 likely escaped that fix.

7. **TR-10-15 forward reference**: §3 explicitly notes TR-10-15 is not yet published; §4 and §6 still cite it normatively. The parser should not gate any IPMX-JPEG-XS check on TR-10-15 content until TR-10-15 is published and on disk. AMBIGUOUS clauses JX-26 and JX-27 should be revisited when TR-10-15 ships.

8. **PCM Audio §6.1.4 has the exact same bullet-binding shape as JPEG-XS §6.1.4.** PCM-13's bullets (Sample rate / Sample size / Channel count / Packet time / Measured sample rate / Channel order) attach to "shall populate all required PCM Audio Media Info Block fields as defined in TR-10-3, including:" — they are MIB fields, NOT SDP attributes. If the parser were ever tempted to add a `channel order` SDP-form check at the IPMX-PCM tier based on this section, the same trap applies. The SDP-side channel-order mechanism (e.g. `a=channel-order` per ST 2110-30) lives in ST 2110-30, not at the IPMX tier.

9. **Cross-tier cascade**: every IPMX-tier check the parser implements MUST first pass ST 2110 (which itself first passes RFC 4566). The IPMX layer's own additions are mostly NMOS, MIB, and device-capability — leaving very little for the SDP-only validator to enforce. This is consistent with CLAUDE.md's Validation Strictness Principle.

10. **No IPMX-specific `a=` attribute additions found in any of the three profile docs.** No new fmtp parameter names. No new sampling-mode values. No new colorimetry values. No new HDR signaling SDP attributes. (HDR / privacy / HDCP are exclusively cross-referenced as out-of-SDP-scope or absent.) The previous parse_sdp work that removed opinion-based IPMX SDP checks (commits f6aa63f and the audit D2 finding) is consistent with the contents of these v1.0 released profile documents.
